Current Commentary

Thoughts After Reading the Report of the British Industrial Mission

Yesterday's foreign dispatch reported that the naval disarmament conference between the United Kingdom, the United States, and Japan has officially adjourned, indicating that future negotiations will likely occur outside the conference setting. Regarding the Far Eastern issue, which is of global concern, in addition to the development of US-Japan relations, the evolution of UK-Japan relations will be a decisive factor in the Pacific diplomatic landscape. The weight of the UK's position cannot be overstated. After reviewing the report on the Manchuria survey released yesterday by the British Industrial Association, we cannot help but feel certain emotions.

The balance of power among Far Eastern nations has been disrupted since Japan's occupation of the four northeastern provinces of China during the September 18th Incident, coupled with the April 17, 1934 declaration that "other countries cannot interfere." This has inevitably caused alarm among the United Kingdom and the United States, with the United States' attitude towards Japan being particularly pronounced. To this day, US representative Davis still clings to the maintenance of the Nine-Power Treaty (London dispatch on the 20th). It is clear that he is unwilling to completely abandon his ambition in the Far East. The United Kingdom, caught in the middle, faces a more difficult situation. While it has not failed to express sympathy for Davis's position, it cannot avoid engaging with Japan. We can already glimpse the UK's intentions from the previous Lytton Report. The declaration upon the departure of the British inspection team and the report after their return repeatedly stated that their actions were non-official and non-political, only aiming to promote a permanent link between London and Tokyo and to strengthen the spirit of friendship. Their efforts can be imagined. However, the UK's traditional diplomatic approach is also like this.

Some say that the British inspection team's long journey overseas was nothing more than a guise of commercial negotiations to seek political compromise, a kind of diplomatic strategy. Whether this is true, we do not want to speculate at first. However, judging from the general content of this report, it focuses on cooperation and development of "Manchukuo" as the fundamental spirit for enhancing UK-Japan relations. It does not view Japan's policies as erroneous. Although it does not comment on Japan's recent activities in "Man-Meng" (Manchuria and Mongolia), its expression of sympathy towards Japan can be glimpsed. However, we have one point of suspicion regarding this British inspection team's visit to "Manchuria." In terms of UK trade relations with "Manchuria," in 1933, Japan held the top position in trade with "Manchuria," followed by Germany and the United States. However, "Manchuria's" exports to the UK amounted to 9 million "Manchukuo yuan," while imports from the UK were only over 7 million "Manchukuo yuan." "Manchuria" clearly had a trade surplus with the UK. Moreover, since "Manchuria" announced a petroleum monopoly, and recently revised import tariffs, the future development of the "Manchurian" market, from the perspective of the great powers, except for Japan, has become increasingly bleak and is hardly a central focus of the UK's overseas market. Now, looking at its report, although it is cited as a good opportunity for development, considering the guarantee of cooperative principles and the hope for the establishment of a steel agreement, its gains will certainly not be substantial. If such hard work and long-distance inspections only yield such results, is this the best strategy for the British? We believe that, with the UK's intelligence, its intentions must extend beyond this.

Soviet Russia Discovers Fascist Terrorist Organization

Two High-Ranking Officials Suddenly Arrested

Related to the Kirov Assassination Case

Russian Government's Excessive Executions Shock British Labour Party

(London) A correspondent for the Daily Mail in Warsaw cabled today that, according to Moscow radio reports, two former high-ranking Soviet officials have been arrested in connection with the Kirov assassination case. This matter has been confirmed. The two arrested are Zinoviev, former Secretary-General of the Third International, and Kamenev, former Ambassador to Italy. After meeting with Stalin and leaving the Kremlin, Stalin immediately ordered their arrest. Stalin later announced via radio that he would not rest until the opposition party members of these two were completely eliminated. Zinoviev and Kamenev had previously been expelled from Russia twice for opposing Stalin. This arrest occurred on Thursday, and the charges against them are for the murder of Kirov. After describing the arrest, the radio reporter said, "We now at least know who the enemy is." According to another report from the Daily Telegraph's Moscow correspondent, the truth about the recent work stoppages in Russia may come to light after the arrest of Zinoviev and Kamenev. The correspondent also stated that a Fascist terrorist organization has been discovered within the opposition party. Observers believe that this speculation is based on recent editorials published by the Moscow Soviet newspaper Izvestia, one of the most important phrases being "The former opposition in the party has now mutated into counter-revolutionary Fascists." According to reports a few days ago, Zinoviev had regained his former position and been appointed to an important position in the Ministry of Education. (National News Agency dispatch on the 21st)

(London) According to Warsaw sources, Zinoviev and Kamenev, who both assisted Lenin in creating the Soviet Union, have now been arrested at home. Moscow has neither confirmed nor denied this claim. It is noted that the collapse of the first British Labour government in 1924 was due to a letter from Zinoviev. This letter, disclosed by newspapers, caused the Labour government to lose the trust of the people because it encouraged the British Communist Party to revolt. Kamenev, originally named Rosenfeld, was elected Chairman of the Council of Labour and Defence Administration after Lenin's death. He was later dismissed for joining the opposition party led by Trotsky. The British Labour Party has been quite shocked by the recent executions in Russia. The General Council of the Trades Union Congress and the National Executive Committee of the Labour Party have passed a resolution stating that Russia's retaliatory measures involving indiscriminate killings since Kirov's assassination are alarming. Those detained should be allowed to defend themselves in accordance with the law and be given a public trial. A delegation will be appointed to visit the Russian Ambassador to the United Kingdom, and the Labour Party's daily newspaper, the Daily Herald, condemns Russia's actions as barbaric and unsuitable for civilized nations. (Reuters dispatch on the 21st)

Philippine Police Board Russian Cargo Ship and Arrest People

Twenty-Three People, Including Overseas Chinese

Captain Protests to the US and Philippine Governments

Manila: The captain of the Soviet cargo ship "Vokjoniki資號," Mushuv, protested to the US and Philippine governments today because Philippine police boarded the ship and arrested 23 residents of Manila, and non-police forcibly returned Russians to the ship. However, authorities claim that those arrested are Philippine and Chinese communists funded by Moscow. If possible, they will be prosecuted for communist activities. (Reuters dispatch on the 21st)

British Industrial Association Approves Report

And Establishes a Committee

(London) The British Industrial Association held an important meeting here today, chaired by Scott, and unanimously approved the report of the Japan-Manchuria survey team. The association also immediately established a standing committee as the first step in UK-Japan business cooperation. The chairman of the committee is Sir Barnby, and the members include Sir Sillyman of the Sillyman Brothers' Bank, British Industrial Association Director Roacock, and British copper and iron industry representative Picator. The committee will discuss economic issues affecting the UK and Japan with a similar committee from the Japan Economic Association, paying particular attention to commercial competition and the development of commerce in "Manchukuo" by the UK and Japan. At the meeting, Sir Barnby presented the report, and other members of the Far East survey team sat quietly on the podium. (National News Agency dispatch on the 20th)

(London) The London Times and the Morning Post today both summarized and published the report of the delegation sent by the British Industrial Federation to inspect "Manchukuo" and added comments. Both newspapers welcomed the view expressed at the end of the report that cooperation between the British and Japanese business communities is necessary. The Times said that reasonable adjustments could benefit both countries, and the Morning Post said that the general atmosphere of goodwill created by this trip was the most valuable result of the inspection team. (Reuters dispatch on the 21st)

Serious Silver Problem: US Receives Another Document from Russia

Ambassador Shi Continues to Submit Several Notes

The State Department Immediately Holds Several Meetings

(Washington) The State Department is now considering correspondence from China regarding the US government's silver purchasing program. According to Secretary of State Hull today, several more letters have been received from Chinese Ambassador Shi regarding this issue. Reports have also come from Ambassador Bullitt to Russia and Minister Johnson to China, who recently traveled to China. The State Department has also received documents from other sources. Hull did not indicate whether the US government will take any action soon, nor did he disclose the contents of the documents. (Reuters dispatch on the 20th)

(Washington) Government officials, Minister Johnson to China, and Ambassador Bullitt to Russia have met several times to discuss the impact of the US government's silver plan on the Far East, paying particular attention to the situation in China. Secretary of State Hull declared that they had discussed all aspects of the silver plan and related economic issues. Johnson and Bullitt are both here now, but will soon return to their original posts. When asked whether the Chinese government had recently sent another note to the US government regarding the US silver purchase plan, Hull was evasive but said that they occasionally exchanged views on various economic issues but declined to answer definitively. It is noted that the Chinese Ministry of Finance has sent several notes to the US in the past month, asking it to explain its attitude toward the silver policy and explain the impact of the US silver purchase plan on China. As for the opinions of Senate leaders regarding the policies that should be adopted in the future, they are quite divided. (National News Agency dispatch on the 20th)

(Washington) Since the implementation of the silver policy, China's silver reserves have gradually decreased, causing a threat to the financial and economic situation. The Chinese government has recently requested that the US State Department and Treasury Department cooperate to remedy this situation. According to reports, in October of this year, China suggested to the United States that it exchange Chinese silver for US cash in order to gradually adopt the gold standard and avoid rising silver prices, but this was politely refused by the United States. (Havas dispatch on the 21st)

US Forms China Economic Inspection Team, to Arrive in Shanghai from New York Early Next Year

Dozens of Business Leaders from China and the US are Working to Promote Trade Between the Two Countries

(New York) The US International Trade Association announced today that 15 to 25 US international trade leaders and experts will form a China Economic Survey Team. The team will depart from New York for Shanghai early next year, collect materials in China for at least three months, and then return home to submit a report and propose ways to promote US-China trade. According to International Trade Association President Thomas, the Shanghai US-China Trade Association is assisting in this effort. The Shanghai US-China Trade Association was organized by six Chinese leaders and six US banking and business leaders in the Far East. The list of the survey team has not yet been released. When they go to China, they will lead a large number of secretaries familiar with collecting materials. All organizations are now being handled by the New York US-China Trade Association. The scope, nature, and distance of the journey of previous economic or trade survey groups cannot be compared with the organization of this event. Therefore, international trade experts are paying close attention to the results of the team. If the results are good, similar survey teams may go to other places. The Shanghai US-China Trade Association was established on September 15 of this year and specializes in cooperating with similar organizations in the US to develop US-China trade. The chairman of the association is Zhang Jia'ao, President of the China International Trade Association and General Manager of the Bank of China. The vice chairman is Franklin, Vice Chairman and Accountant of Shanghai Shenchang & Co. Other American members include Hawkins, Chairman of the Power Company, Basseid of Xiangmei Tobacco Company, Schmeyer, Vice President of Chase Bank, Gobert, Deputy Manager of Mobil Oil Company, Potter, Deputy Manager of Da Lai Foreign Company, and Anott, US Commercial Counselor to China, who is an honorary American member. Chinese members include Lin Kanghou, General Director of the Bankers' Association and the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, Chen Guangfu, General Manager of Shanghai Bank, Yu Zuoting, Chairman of the General Chamber of Commerce, Guo Bingwen, General Manager of Shanghai Trust Company, Chen Zhezheng, Manager of Yanye Bank, and He Bingxian, Director of the International Trade Bureau of the Ministry of Industry, who is an honorary Chinese member. (National News Agency dispatch on the 20th)

Japan Establishes Diplomatic Inspectors

Planning to Expand New Markets Abroad

(Tokyo) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs previously appointed Ambassador Yoshida Shigeru as Representative of Foreign Minister Hirota, and sent him to various countries to connect the diplomatic camps at home and abroad. The results were quite effective. In view of this, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs decided to establish a permanent system of foreign affairs inspectors. Foreign Minister Hirota is now considering specific matters such as personnel selection and inspection areas. The first inspection areas are Southeast Asia, India, Central Asia, Africa, and Central and South America. These are all new markets for Japan's foreign trade, so the mission of the inspectors is also very important. It is heard that Foreign Minister Hirota intends to recommend former Ambassador to Italy Matsushima or former Ambassador to Brazil Hayashi. (Japan United Press dispatch on the 21st)

French-Russian Political Cooperation

(Moscow) The Izvestia newspaper editorial, titled "French-Soviet Political Cooperation," stated: "The Eastern Regional Pact proposed by France and the Soviet Union will guarantee that if any country in Eastern Europe is invaded, mutual assistance will be provided. This is well known. The pact includes Germany, Poland, the Soviet Union, Latvia, Estonia, and Lithuania, and guarantees their integrity to each signatory. This consolidates peace in Eastern Europe and the entire Europe. However, it is well known that some countries have resisted the signing of this pact. Judging from the protocol signed by Litvinov and Laval on December 5, it can be seen that the struggle to conclude this pact cannot end here. In this context, the French and Soviet governments are aware that any attempt to conclude agreements to replace the Eastern Regional Pact or that are contrary to the nature of this pact must be met with opposition. German foreign policy has always completely separated the problem of resolving contradictions in Western Europe from the problem of endangering peace in Eastern Europe. The reason why the aforementioned France and the Soviet Union have this attitude is that France and the Soviet Union deeply know that this kind of policy is extremely dangerous for general peace. Those who want to sacrifice the peace interests of a part of Europe and resolve the contradictions in another part are creating a historical avenue of continuous war, and some countries are constantly referred to as sworn enemies. As for the Soviet attitude, Litvinov has already stated it very clearly in his speech on the 7th of this month, 'It is always willing to establish excellent relations with Germany in all aspects.' The Soviet Union has no motive to isolate Germany while conducting diplomatic cooperation with France. The publication of the French-Soviet protocol has made the world aware of the truth. The protocol first mentions the increase in diplomatic cooperation between the French and Soviet governments, and at the same time, it is necessary to notify each other of proposals that may hinder the conclusion of the aforementioned pact and attempt to consolidate peace. From this point of view, some newspapers hostile to French-Soviet friendship falsely claim that this protocol has a limited and obstructive effect on the struggle to promote French-Soviet relations. It can be seen that this is a baseless rumor. The French and Soviet governments will never form a group in an attempt to deal with other countries. They are only concerned with how to organize peace in a way that benefits all countries. Therefore, they are willing to provide other governments that express their willingness to work for peace with the opportunity to actually join the Eastern Regional Pact to prove that what they say is not false. Only the Eastern Pact can enhance relations between Eastern European countries and remove an obstacle to peace in Western Europe." (TASS dispatch on the 20th)

Unrest on the Russian-Manchu Border

Boli (Khabarovsk): Several provocative incidents of Manchu forces shooting at Soviet guards occurred in the Soviet-Manchu border area near Hailanpao (Blagoveshchensk) at the end of November and the beginning of December. For example, on November 28, Soviet border guard Korneev, when stationed on the Soviet border 5 kilometers from the village of Bibikovo, was suddenly shot at with rifles by several unidentified people from the Manchu territory. On December 2, a Soviet guard was again shot at by Manchu forces 4 kilometers from Verkny-Hailanpao. The perpetrators fled into the mountains. On December 4, a Soviet guard was shot at by Manchu forces near Sakhalin. The bullets flew over his head. The guard narrowly escaped death due to coincidence under other combined circumstances. The Soviet consul in Sakhalin has now protested to the Manchu negotiators regarding these cross-border incidents. (Havas dispatch on the 20th)

Puppet State Salt Monopoly

To Be Implemented After Survey Completed Next Year

(Changchun) "Manchukuo's" salt tax system has so far inherited the system from the old regime, divided into the Salt Affairs Office, which collects salt taxes, and the Jihei Transport Office, which has a monopoly purpose. However, due to the implementation of the new administrative fee system, if the salt affairs system is not reformed, it will only make matters complicated and hinder control. Therefore, the financial authorities are now studying the advantages and disadvantages of the two, and as a result, they may adopt a monopoly system. After the survey is completed, the salt monopoly system may be implemented next year. (Denstu dispatch on the 21st)

Belgium and Norway Violate the Ban on Supplying Arms to Bolivia and Paraguay

The UK Asks the League of Nations to Pay Attention

The Advisory Committee Convenes a Meeting

(London) The UK recently approached the League of Nations, stating that Belgium and Norway had violated the League of Nations Administrative Council resolution by transporting arms to the Chaco region. The Secretariat of the League of Nations was asked to pay attention. It is understood that this approach is entirely a notification. (Havas dispatch on the 20th)

(Geneva) The Advisory Committee organized by the League of Nations for the Chaco dispute held its final meeting this morning to discuss a letter from the British government. The British letter reported to the League of Nations that Belgium and Norway had violated the League of Nations Administrative Council resolution by privately transporting arms to Bolivia and Paraguay. Among them, the transfer of arms to the ports of Collica in Chile and Montevide in Uruguay was particularly important. The committee decided that if Bolivia and Paraguay still did not provide a satisfactory answer to the recommendations put forward by the League of Nations General Assembly by January 14 next year, corresponding measures should be taken to strictly implement the original arms embargo. (Havas dispatch on the 21st)

Oslo: The authorities here recently announced that Norway had entered into contracts with foreign countries before the League of Nations Administrative Council passed the ban on arms to the Chaco (May 19 of this year). The arms and ammunition that have been continuously exported since then are in accordance with the provisions of the contract. (Havas dispatch on the 21st)

UK and US Actively Develop Aviation

Planning Regular Airmail Services between the UK, Philippines, and Australia

The Entire Plan to Be Completed Within Two Years

US-Made Giant Aircraft to Fly the Pacific

(London) Under-Secretary of State for Air Sassoon outlined the UK's grand plans for the development of air transport in the Empire in the Lower House today, saying that the plans were drawn up by the Air Ministry in conjunction with various airline companies in the Empire. The main features are threefold: First, the actual improvement of air schedules between certain parts of the Empire. Second, a significant increase in the number of air services. Third, the convenience of first-class mail being delivered by aircraft at the same rate as existing ordinary postage fees. Currently, this matter is purely temporary because the plan depends on the cooperation of governments throughout the Empire. According to this plan, mail to India will take only two days and a bit, East Africa will take two and a half days, South Africa and Singapore will each take three days, and Australia will take seven days. Mail planes will fly to India about four or five times a week, Singapore and East Africa three times each, and South Africa and Australia twice each. The plan also contains a large-scale program for developing the basic organization of air routes throughout the Empire, so that aircraft not only carry mail but also passengers, and not only travel during the day but also fly at night. As for the financial and aircraft type details, he is currently unable to release them as he is still engaged in negotiations with other relevant governments. The date on which this plan will be implemented has not been determined, but it is expected to be fully implemented within two years. There may not be a 3.5 pence postage fee before 1937. (Reuters dispatch on the 20th)

(London) According to a report in the News, major British aircraft factories have recently partnered with the Air Ministry to build several airships for regular air service between the UK and Canada. Once the airships are successful, they can fly directly from the UK to Newfoundland without stopping and can carry passengers and mail. (National News Agency dispatch on the 20th)

Baltimore, USA: Pan American Airlines previously planned to use giant seaplanes for transpacific flights in order to open a regular air route between the US and China. These seaplanes are being built in the city. One aircraft, named "Flying Boat," has been completed. The maximum speed of this aircraft is 290 kilometers per hour, the normal speed is 257 kilometers per hour, and it can carry 48 passengers. (Havas dispatch on the 20th)

US Defense of the Panama Canal Area Strengthened

Sufficient to Cope with Emergencies

(Washington) Army and Navy officers stated today that the naval and military strength in the Panama Canal area is sufficient to cope with emergencies. They expressed great attention to the claim by the owner of the Panama American magazine, Lance Valls, that the canal zone's defense works were weak. However, they stated that Valls may have overemphasized the possibility of attacks and underestimated the defensive forces that could be quickly concentrated after an order was given. Valls had claimed that "twenty daredevils could blow up the canal," and it would take months to restore navigation. Army officials only admitted that they were powerless to stop two ships loaded with explosives from simultaneously entering the canal from both ends and detonating at the locks. Self-sacrificing aviators could also temporarily disable the locks. However, to prevent this from happening, the Army is currently planning to install huge steel wire nets above the locks as soon as funding is secured. (20th National Telegram)

Germany is Unprepared for Aerial Warfare; Britain Should Not Overthink It

International Cooperation is Desired

Göring's Remarks to British Reporters

(Berlin) Prussian Prime Minister and Minister of Aviation Göring told a Reuters reporter today that Germany does not have the technical means to carry out aerial attacks. Britain's fear of being harmed by Germany from the sky is an overestimation. The German people yearn for Britain and Germany to maintain a sincere friendship on an equal footing, and this comes purely from nature. He believes that international problems next year can all be resolved peacefully. The German government has no other wish than to seek progress through peace and international cooperation. Göring continued to address the issue of German rearmament, saying that if other countries develop armaments for aerial warfare, Germany should at least be allowed the right to make the necessary preparations to ensure the safety of the German people. However, if other countries are willing to abolish their military aircraft fleets, Germany is also very willing to do the same. Göring then declared that the German people are now behind the National Socialist government and denied rumors of disagreement among cabinet members. Finally, he said that although Germany's economic situation is as serious as anywhere else in the world, it has recently made great progress. This is due to the genius of German scientists and inventors in gradually overcoming the lack of raw materials. (20th Reuters Dispatch)

French and German Veterans Strive for Peaceful Cooperation

Pleasant Talks in Berlin

Not Involving Political Issues

(Berlin) Veteran soldiers from Germany and France are jointly engaged in peace talks, which resumed in Berlin today. The French representatives include Mr. Bichot, president of the French veterans' organization "Federal Group," and Secretary Landou. However, both sides stated that these talks are specifically designed to establish honorable peace and cooperation between the two countries and do not involve any important political issues. Currently, Bichot and Landou remain in Berlin to continue the talks and have also met with German leader Hitler and Deputy Prime Minister Hess, both of whom are also veterans, so the talks were very pleasant. In the future, all veterans' organizations in Germany and France plan to hold expanded talks, but this will be based on the principle of not interfering with the current talks. (20th National Telegram)

Belgian Authorities Explain Franco-Belgian Military Agreement

In the Event of Trouble in Europe, Belgian Troops Have No Obligation to be Deployed to France

French Troops May Not Pass Through Belgian Territory Unless Requested

Brussels Minister Pouille gave a speech explaining the Franco-Belgian military agreement, stating that Belgium is not subject to any constraints from France. This was considered provocative by political circles. Pouille later stated that it is completely incorrect that, according to the agreement, Belgium would have to participate if Germany and France were to come into conflict, because a military agreement and a military alliance are two different things. The agreement stipulates that French troops may not enter Belgian territory unless requested by Belgium, and Belgian troops have no obligation to be deployed to France. It can only be said that Belgium would automatically join the war if it so chose. Pouille promoted the Franco-Belgian military agreement in 1920, but he was never willing to take the great risk of granting France the right to demand the mobilization of Belgian troops in the event of a Franco-German conflict. (20th National Telegram)

New Yugoslav Cabinet Formed

Prime Minister Jevtić Concurrently Holds Foreign Affairs Portfolio

Belgrade Former Foreign Minister Jevtić has formed a new cabinet today on a broad basis, including eight Serbians, four Croatians, two Slovenians, and one Muslim. Jevtić is highly respected in the country. Although he now serves as Prime Minister, he still holds the position of Foreign Minister concurrently. (11th Reuters Dispatch)

British-Australian Race: Second Place

Dutch Plane Crashes in Desert

Crashed While En Route to the East Indies After Hitting a Power Line

Four Crew Members and Three Passengers Killed

The Hague The Dutch plane Douglas FG-2, piloted by aviators Bazitiel and Moore, participated in the British-Australian air race in October, resulting in second place. This plane departed from here yesterday, planning to fly to Batavia, Java, Dutch East Indies, but crashed in the desert near Rutbah, Syria, due to engine malfunction. This morning, the three-engine plane "Scheepshol" flew out from here to join the search. (21st Havas Dispatch)

Baghdad The Dutch plane Uiver was found today by a British plane in the desert ten miles from Rutbah. All four crew members and three passengers were dead. Representatives of the Dutch airline rushed to the scene upon hearing the tragic news. The crash site is 250 miles from here. The deceased passengers were identified as Pelledey, manager of the Dutch East Indies news agency, Professor Hua Zhi of Batavia, and a merchant named Kourt. The plane is thought to have crashed in the desert after hitting a power line. According to a Reuters dispatch from Amsterdam, this plane previously ranked second in the British-Australian air speed race, and Dutch people attached great importance to it. They are extremely saddened by the news of its crash. Fortunately, the pilots who participated in the race on this plane, Pimentel and Moore, did not take this flight. (21st Reuters Dispatch)

The Hague Grief spread throughout the Dutch East Indies and the Netherlands upon hearing the news of the crash of the plane Uiver. Both places are now flying flags at half-mast and have stopped broadcasting on radio stations. The deaths of Pelledey and Professor Hua Zhi are particularly lamented. Pelledey was famous in the Dutch press, and Hua was renowned in the medical community. Hua, a well-known expert in tropical diseases, often presided over international conferences in Singapore. He only flew to the Netherlands last week to visit his sick mother. Among the deceased crew members, chief pilot Pikman had flown approximately 10,000 hours in his lifetime. Wireless operator Zietelhoef was the only survivor in the 1931 crash of the plane Stork near Bangkok. The Dutch authorities are very grateful to the British Royal Air Force for their assistance in searching for the Uiver and have sent a thank you note to the British Air Ministry today. (21st Reuters Dispatch)

Saarland Voting Order

Voting to be Held on January 13 Next Year

Eighty-Three Districts, Eight Hundred and Sixty Polling Places

Saarbrücken According to the latest voting order drafted by the Voting Committee, the results of the public vote on January 13 next year will not be revealed until the early morning of the 15th at the earliest. The committee has also drafted concrete measures to ensure the security of the ballot boxes, so that each ballot box will be securely sealed after voting ends in each city. It will be escorted by the military to the Saarbrücken counting center, to avoid any accidents during transit. Heavy troops and armored vehicles will protect it along the way. This vote is divided into 83 districts, with 860 polling stations. Each station will be guarded and monitored by 960 foreign nationals. These foreigners were specially recruited for the polling stations, with the majority being from the Netherlands and Switzerland. Based on the recommendation of the Voting Committee, it is proposed to designate December 23-27 as a Christmas political truce period. All political propaganda will be suspended during the truce. This proposal has now been approved by all political parties. The Voting Committee has announced its implementation today, and newspapers that do not belong to any political party have also been notified by the committee not to publish any political propaganda or advocacy work during the Christmas period. (20th National Telegram)

Army Drills to Be Held Simultaneously

(London) British Prime Minister MacDonald announced in the House of Commons today the preparations for the celebration of the 25th anniversary of the British Emperor's accession on May 6 next year. He said that the Emperor will receive the diplomatic corps and representatives from all parts of the British Empire during the celebration and will receive congratulatory messages from both houses of Parliament. The Emperor and Queen also plan to travel by carriage through various parts of London, receiving congratulations from the people. The Emperor also stated that the Prince of Wales will represent the Emperor at the celebration in Wales. In addition to the decorations in various government offices, army drills will be held during the celebration. (21st Reuters Dispatch)

Citroen Automobile Company Declares Liquidation Due to Poor Business

20,000 People Will Lose Their Jobs as a Result

A Major Impact on the Social Economy

(Paris) Citroen Automobile Company, with a capital of 400 million francs and producing 35 percent of the nation's automobiles, one of France's most important factories, has decided to temporarily close its doors during the Christmas holidays due to financial difficulties. However, it will reopen in the future. Because the factory employs 20,000 workers, and about 50,000 family members depend on it for their livelihood, if they lose their jobs, it will lead to social unrest and trigger economic repercussions in other areas. The House of Representatives still firmly believes that the government should not use public funds to help private businesses, but financial experts believe that the factory cannot be maintained without government guarantees. Furthermore, the factory owes a large amount of taxes, and the government is likely the largest creditor. It is expected that the Citroen company will conduct its own liquidation, reduce capital, reorganize, and then raise new loans. (21st Reuters Dispatch)

(Paris) The Seine Provincial Commercial Court, after conducting an investigation into the business situation of the Citroen Automobile Company, has decided to declare liquidation. Labor unions are deeply concerned that if the company closes down and workers lose their jobs, there will be a major impact on society. This morning, Secretary Shih Wu of the General Labor Union led a delegation to visit Labor Minister Jacques, requesting that various measures be taken to avoid laying off workers. Some members of the Orthodox Socialist Party in the House of Representatives plan to raise questions about the Citroen company's liquidation in the afternoon, demanding a government response. (21st Havas Dispatch)

Mountrie Silver Today in the Mountrie silver market, its goods fell about 60 pounds.

Exchange Rates

British-American Today (December 21) morning, there was little trading in the London foreign exchange market. The opening price of the British-American exchange rate was 4 yuan 9 jiao 3 fen 9375, which was 0.0625 higher than yesterday's closing price of the US-British exchange rate. The Interpretation of Uncertainties in the Army, Navy, and Air Force Criminal Law and Trial Law

(Nanjing) Regarding the case where the Taiyuan Pacification Headquarters requested an interpretation of uncertainties in the Army, Navy, and Air Force Criminal Law and Trial Law, the Judicial Yuan provides the following explanation: (1) Forcibly conscripting people into the military, as there is no explicit provision in the Army, Navy, and Air Force Criminal Law, should be handled according to Article 318 of the Criminal Law. If there are circumstances under Article 316 of the Criminal Law, that article should be applied for sentencing. (2) Failing to report the full quota constitutes a crime under Article 40 of the Army, Navy, and Air Force Criminal Law, without the need for other conditions. (3) Those who intend to re-claim expenses by falsely reporting the number of personnel, regardless of whether the expenses have been claimed or not, should be punished according to Article 45 of the Army, Navy, and Air Force Criminal Law. (4) The "order or command" mentioned in Article 64 of the same law refers to matters pertaining to military affairs, and there is no distinction made between written or verbal forms. As for "resisting orders" or "disobeying commands," both active and passive actions can constitute the offense. (5) The provisions of Article 72 of the same law refer to gatherings of a multitude that engage in violence or coercion, and do not conform to the circumstances of Articles 66 to 71 of the same law. (6) Since Article 77 of the same law does not have provisions for failing to comply, those who steal bombs but do not sell them, or steal them and fail to sell them, should be punished according to Article 85 of the same law. (7) The "fabrication of rumors to mislead the public" mentioned in Article 92 of the same law is limited to matters concerning military affairs. If one verbally impersonates a military officer to solicit military matters, it should be considered as fabricating rumors to mislead the public. (8) Inducing soldiers from other camps to desert and enlisting them into one's own camp should be punished according to Article 163 of the Criminal Law. (9) If soldiers seize property or engage in gang robbery, and Chapter 10 of the Army, Navy, and Air Force Criminal Law has no public rights provisions, public rights should not be deprived. (10) Whether Article 39 of the Army, Navy, and Air Force Trial Law has missing text is not within the scope of interpretation and should not be answered. A letter will be sent for reference. (21st Special Dispatch)

General Conditions of the Silver and Money Industry in the Capital

(Nanjing) The silver and money industry is required to have a general closing at the end of each year. The general closing of the silver and money industry in the capital is following the government's order to be completed by the end of this month. As for the date of the general transfer of funds, because the transactions of commercial firms are mostly settled at the end of the old lunar year, there is no way to raise current funds before the due date. Therefore, the debts and credits of the silver and money industry cannot be collected and transferred until the end of the old lunar year. Therefore, the formal closing is done according to the national calendar, but it is only a formality. The date of the general transfer of funds will still follow the old lunar calendar. Furthermore, the money industry in this city will not suffer losses this year apart from expenses, nor will there be any surplus. (21st Special Dispatch)

Jiangsu Province Reforms Grain Payment System

Starting First with Counties That Have Completed Land Reporting

Tax Collection Offices to Be Established by Local Banks to Handle Payments

Zhenjiang dispatch: The Jiangsu Finance Department, in view of the fact that in the past, the collection of grain taxes in various counties of the province was handled by the county government's grain treasury, and the drawbacks were countless, although strict punishment was imposed once discovered, it was ultimately impossible to completely eliminate them. In order to reform this, it is planned to entrust the collection of grain taxes to local banks. The money will be collected by the banks at tax collection offices established at the local county government, and they will directly handle the payments with the grain households, starting first with counties that have completed land reporting. According to sources from the Finance Department, the implementation of this system has been successful in seven counties, including Wuxian, Changshu, Kunshan, Jiading, Yixing, and Wujiang. In Zhenjiang, it will be implemented in January next year. This is truly a major reform in the tax administration. The tax payment methods are recorded below:

In the preliminary stage of paying taxes, taxpayers should submit their land deeds or old account books to the counter in the collection district to calculate the amount payable. The collection office will fill out a tax payment notice and return it to the taxpayer along with the land deeds. The taxpayer will then take these to the tax collection office to pay the amount. The tax collection office will collect the amount according to the number, fill out a tax receipt, and issue it to the taxpayer as proof of claiming the land deed. The tax collection office will make three copies of the tax receipt: one copy will be kept as a file copy, one copy (blue) will be given to the taxpayer as proof of receipt, and one copy (red) will be sent directly by the tax collection office to the land deed office to be used for verifying the issuance of land deeds. After the land deed office issues the return deed, the blue copy will be attached to the return deed, filed, and kept for future reference. The red copy will be stamped with a "Return Deed Received" seal and sent to the collection office for registration in the account books. If there is an error in the tax calculation, the land deed office, upon discovering it when issuing the land deed, will, if there is an overpayment, fill out a tax refund notice and send it to the collection office for verification and approval, and then take it to the tax collection office to refund the overpaid tax. The original tax receipt will be stamped with a "Tax Refunded" seal. If there is an underpayment, then the tax will be made up and a supplementary tax receipt will be written as proof.

Shandong Treasures: Qingzhou Peaches and Laiyang Pears

Yantai Fruit Products Known Throughout the World

Shandong Construction Department Investigates Production and Sales Conditions

Jinan correspondence: Shandong is rich in native products. In addition to important native products such as cotton, wheat, and peanuts, there are famous fruits everywhere, such as Feicheng peaches, Leling dates, Caozhou pomegranates, Qingzhou honey peaches, Laiyang pears, etc., all of which are famous north of Hebei and surpass Jiangnan in taste. The Construction Department previously sent personnel to investigate the production and sales conditions of various fruits, as well as their diseases, in order to prevent them. The investigation report on Qingzhou honey peaches, Laiyang pears, Yantai fruits, etc. in eastern Shandong has now been completed. The following is an excerpt of the part about production and sales:

Laiyang Pears

(1) Production area and area: The cultivation area of Laiyang pears is limited to the sandy land on the east bank of the Xian River and the south bank of the Zhang River. The villages on the east bank of the Xian River where pears are planted include Wu Gezhuang, Hongtuya, Yangergang, Zhaowangzhuang, and Yejiabo, extending from Wulong Village in the south to Shipeng in the north, about ten li long. The villages on the south bank of the Zhang River where pears are planted include Yun Gezhuang, Lu Gezhuang, Lu'erkou, Dataozhang, and Xitaozhang, extending from Nanwu to Su Gezhuang, about twenty-five li long. This area is the most abundant area for pear production. The soil in all the pear orchards in both places is pure quartz sand, and the deeper the sand layer, the better the quality of the pears. Therefore, the pears produced in areas with deep sand layers in Lu'erkou, Zhaowangzhuang, and Yejiabo have been valuable fruits since ancient times. People from various countries in the East and West are now competing to buy them, and gourmand nearby also do not hesitate to spend huge sums of money to buy them. Therefore, the reputation of Laiyang pears in the eastern Shandong area is no less than that of the Feitao peach in western Shandong. The following is an estimate of the area and number of plants in each village with more orchards: Lu'erkou 200 mu, 3,000 plants; Dataozhang 300 mu, 4,500 plants; Wu Gezhuang 400 mu, 6,000 plants; Xin Gezhuang 300 mu, 4,500 plants; Yuan Gezhuang 250 mu, 3,750 plants; Lu'ergang 900 mu, 13,500 plants; Zhaowangzhuang 700 mu, 10,500 plants; Yejiabo 300 mu, 4,500 plants; Nanwu 50 mu, 75 plants; Zhou Gezhuang 200 mu, 3,000 plants; Xitaozhang 200 mu, 3,000 plants; other villages 250 mu, 375 plants; totaling 4,050 mu, 60,750 plants.

(2) Types and quality: There are about ten types of Laiyang pears, such as Ren Pear, Fragrant Pear, Qiubai Pear, Western Pear, Horseshoe Yellow Pear, Sour Wo Pear, Sweet Wo Pear, Bald Pear, Jimo Pear, Lada Qiu Pear, White Yuan Pear, etc. However, the names of these types have not been studied by scholars, so there is no basis for them. Therefore, only the names used locally are listed. The quality of Ren Pear is the best, with a production volume of more than 70%. Qiubai Pear, Horseshoe Yellow Pear, and White Yuan Pear are next.

(3) Pruning and fertilization: Pear farmers in Laiyang plant about fifteen trees per mu. The branches and trunks are short and the trees spread out low. The tree shape is quite neat. Every spring, mature trees only have their dead and overgrown branches pruned. From March to April, pit fertilizer (commonly known as pit holes) or manure is applied, with the topsoil being dug up and mixed with it. In winter, they are watered with urine.

(4) Production, price, and sales: 1. Production: Pear trees can bear fruit after seven or eight years of planting. Those that are ten years old grow vigorously and have reached their peak fruiting period. According to the locals, some trees are over seventy or eighty years old, and their maximum yield can reach four to five hundred catties. The average yield per tree is about thirty catties. Calculated at fifteen trees per mu, the annual output is 1,822,500 catties (market catty), at 5 cents per catty, totaling 92,25 yuan. 2. Price: The price of Laiyang pears varies depending on the production area and quality. In terms of Ren Pear, the quality of those produced in Lu'ergang and Zhaowangzhuang is the best, and the price is relatively expensive. At this year's market price (September), each catty costs about 5 to 8 cents. Those produced in other villages cost about 3 to 5 cents. If you choose the complete ones without disease or insect damage, the price is often several times higher than the average ones. 3. Transportation and packaging: Since the production of Laiyang pears is as mentioned above and the price is very expensive, except for those with severe disease and insect damage that cannot be sold externally, the excellent ones are sold exclusively in Yantai. Every autumn, farmers temporarily organize small vendor sales associations (referred to as pear vendors), with each group having seven or eight to a dozen people. The main condition for this type of organization is complete credit. Therefore, they are responsible for transportation and sales separately. The first step in the transaction is to contact the pear orchard, designate several pear trees, and when they are ripe, determine the price according to the yield and market price. The timing of payment depends entirely on the credit of both parties and the need for funds. When transporting, they are placed in wicker baskets, surrounded by straw, with each basket weighing 100 catties, and transported by donkeys and mules. It takes three days to travel from Laiyang to Yantai, a distance of 240 li, and the transportation cost is about 3 to 4 yuan.

Qingzhou Honey Peaches

(1) Production Area: Hilly areas are abundant, while plains are extremely scarce, with only a few fragmented patches interspersed among the fields. Therefore, the planting area cannot be accurately estimated. The planting region extends from Yunmen Mountain to Sunwangzhuang in the southwest, a distance of approximately 70 li. To the south, it reaches Yanglaoyuan Village, about 20 li away, to the east it goes to the Mi River, and to the west it reaches Guozhuang, about 50 li. The northern boundary only reaches the vicinity of the Jiaoji Railway. The mountainous areas in the southwest produce peaches that are dry, sweet, and crisp, while those in the north are of lower quality. Therefore, the southwest region can be considered the most suitable area for honey peaches.

(2) Production, Price, and Sales: Peach trees bear fruit after being planted for three to four years. Those aged five to ten years have luxuriant branches and reach their peak fruiting period, yielding an average of about 80 to 100 jin per tree. However, due to the extremely irregular planting, it is difficult to estimate the total production at once. The quantity should be no less than tens of thousands of jin. In August and September, many naturally fall and are sold locally at a price of about two to three cents per jin. Those with bright colors and no significant pest damage are transported and sold to Qingdao, Weixian, Boshan, Jinan, Zhoucun, and other places, with Qingdao being the main market. Last year, about 600 baskets, totaling about 60,000 jin, were transported to Qingdao, with an average price of one dime per jin. During transportation, they are placed in bamboo baskets, surrounded by straw and waste paper, and transported by railway. This year, due to severe insect pests, transportation and sales are extremely unsafe. Many merchants regard it as a dangerous path and dare not engage in it. Therefore, wholesale to other places is only through direct sales by the orchard owners, and the quantity is very small.

Yantai Fruit Products

(1) Production Area and Acreage: Yantai fruit products are abundant, of excellent quality, and renowned far and wide. However, the production area is not limited to the vicinity of Yantai City. Fruit products from Fushan, Muping, Qixia, Laiyang, and other places are all gathered in Yantai and sold to other places. The production area stretches south to Tiekou in Fushan County (about 90 li) and Wangyan (about 40 li), east to Wangdazi Village in Muping County (about 60 li) and Chujiazhuang (about 35 li), and west to Fushan City, directly reaching Qixia. Within this area, due to differences in soil and customs, the planting of fruit trees also varies slightly. Therefore, east of Yantai, grapes are mainly produced. To the west of Muping, pears of the Xiangjiao variety, apples, and Western pears are produced. In the south-central area, rose-scented grapes, pears of the Xiangjiao variety, cherries, and crabapples are mainly produced. In the Wangyan and Tiekou areas, pears of the Xiangjiao variety and Qiu Huapi apples are the most common. To the west, in Qixia, Laiyang pears, Xiangshui pears, pears of the Xiangjiao variety, hawthorns, persimmons, apricots, peaches, and various Chinese cherries are produced. The largest grape orchards are the east and west gardens of Zhang Rong Company, covering an area of about 1,000 mu, with an annual output of 100,000 jin and more than 60 varieties. According to statistics, the area occupied by various fruit orchards, except for a few planted in the plains, is mostly hilly or terraced land, about 150 li from east to west, and scattered in fragments on the hills from north to south. The area cannot be estimated. The largest apple orchard is the Puyuan Orchard in Xishawang, Yantai (founded by Li Zaizhi), covering an area of 150 mu, of which about 90 mu are planted with Xiangjiao, Qiu Huapi, and sweet apples. The trees are vigorous and are at their peak fruiting period.

(2) Types and Quality: There are about a dozen kinds of Yantai fruit products, such as Western pears,

M茄 pears, sweet water pears, Chinese pears, apple varieties such as Xiangjiao, Hongkui, Jinxing Luqing, Qiu Huapi, Fu Huapi, Renqingpi, Baisha Mi, and Pound apples, Chinese apples, sweet apples, crabapple varieties such as Da Haitang, Xiao Haitang, Bai Haitang, grape varieties such as Rose Xiang, Longan, Zhunai, Sweetwater, cherry varieties such as Red Cherry, Yellow Cherry, Black Cherry, and Chinese Cherry, etc. The quality varies slightly depending on the soil and management methods, but Western pears, pears of the Xiangjiao variety, apples, rose-scented grapes, and cherries are the best. The breadth of sales and the height of prices are also the highest. The next best are Qiu Huapi and Fu Huapi apples, and crabapples. (3) Pruning and Fertilization: In the fruit orchards of Yantai, the row and plant spacing for pears, apples, and cherries ranges from one zhang to one zhang five chi. Cup-shaped pruning is mostly used, with short trunks and even distribution of branches. Grapes are pruned horizontally, and the trellises are very simple. Mature fruit trees are pruned of overly dense and dead branches in the spring and autumn seasons. Manure is applied once in March and April, scattered on the ground, and mixed by digging up the topsoil. Urine is poured in winter. In the Zhipu Garden of Xishawang, fish fertilizer is applied in autumn, four to six jin per tree. The amount and quantity of fertilizer applied vary from person to person. Those with more difficult economic conditions may not fertilize, or it is not regular.

(4) Production, Price, and Sales: The annual production of Yantai fruit products is difficult to accurately estimate due to the vast area and distribution throughout Fushan, Laiyang, Muping, and Qixia. As for fruit products, apples are the most common, with pears of the Xiangjiao variety accounting for about 20%, Fu Huapi and Qiu Huapi accounting for about 50%, and Chinese apples accounting for about 10%. Next are Western pears and Chinese pears, accounting for about 10%. Da Qingpi, Baisha Mi, crabapples, grapes, etc., account for about 10%. In recent years, due to soil, climate, and transportation conditions, the fruit orchard industry has expanded, and the fruit production should gradually increase. However, due to sudden climate changes and increased pests and diseases, the number has decreased. The export volume from the 20th to the 22nd years is briefly described below: (1) Shanghai: 10,810,676 jin in the 21st year, and 7,510,275 jin in the 22nd year (sales to Fuzhou, Xiamen, and Hangzhou are also included in this number). (2) Tianjin: 10,388,871 jin in the 21st year, and 667,147 jin in the 22nd year (sales to Peiping are also included in this number). (3) Dalian: 3,164,011 jin in the 21st year, and 5,153,895 jin in the 22nd year. (4) Hong Kong: 1,375,560 jin in the 21st year, and 701,349 jin in the 22nd year. (5) Andong: 1,217,113 jin in the 21st year, and 549,811 jin in the 22nd year. The total is 1,000,002 jin in the 20th year, 17,606,235 jin in the 21st year, and 14,582,488 jin in the 22nd year. The above are the numbers reported by fruit companies to the customs. It is said that about half of each export is not declared for customs duties, because reporting to the customs delays the import and export time, and the fruit products are easily damaged, so it is better to smuggle them and sell them quickly. Based on this calculation, the total export volume of Yantai is not just this number. Also, the export is mainly Qiu Huapi apples, followed by Chinese pears and cherries.

Wuxi

The Xingji Silk Factory Went Bankrupt

The Jiuyu Silk Factory under Kuatang Bridge outside Nanmen had ceased operations for a long time due to the disastrous decline in the silk market and the failure of its operations. In June of this year, villagers such as Ji Yunchu raised funds to continue operations and changed the brand name to Xingji. Recently, Ji Yunchu suddenly absconded to Shanghai with more than 4,000 yuan of silk funds, causing the factory to be unable to make ends meet. Three or forty villagers came to the factory the other day to demand payment for silkworm cocoons. Because Ji avoided coming to the factory, a dispute arose. The female workers and staff in the factory were also concerned that they would not be paid the more than 4,000 yuan owed to them in wages, so they specially elected Shi Wenhui and others as representatives to demand payment from the accounting office. The factory was surrounded on all sides, with no way to maintain operations, and had to announce a shutdown starting yesterday. Now all the employees are increasingly panicked and are prepared to detain the factory's silk. The villagers demanding payment for cocoons are still gathered in the factory and plan to drag the person in charge to the government for assistance.

Bandits Accumulated in Suzhou Arrested in Wuxi

Xu Songbo, a patrol officer from the Fifth Police Station of the Third Public Security Bureau of Suzhou, intercepted two stolen boats in the river under Wangmiao Bridge in the county at about 8 p.m. the night before yesterday and detained six robbers, including Wang Youfu, Qi Laoliu, and Qi Xiaoyang. They confessed that their accomplices, Chen Rongsheng, Wang Liansheng, and Zhu Changfu, were hiding in Wuxi. Patrol Officer Xu then obtained approval from his superiors, came to Wuxi with police documents yesterday, and, together with the Fourth and Fifth Police Bureaus of this county, dispatched police to arrest Chen Rongsheng and Wang Liansheng in a thatched shed near the Third Marine Police Detachment east of Wu Bridge and in a thatched shed near the Maoxin Second Factory. It is reported that Chen and others are all long-time bandits from Taihu Lake and will be sent to Suzhou for interrogation.

Zhenjiang

Dredging of the River Beach Will Begin Soon

The Zhenjiang River Beach Dredging Committee, since jointly designing the dredging of the Zhenjiang River Beach with the Zhenjiang County Construction Bureau, has been planning for many years. All of the first phase of the project, from Pingzheng Bridge to the Puji Wharf and to Zhenjiang Pass, has been designed. Afterwards, due to the time being the tide season, it was inconvenient to construct. Now the committee and others believe that the water has receded during the winter season, and construction should begin in a timely manner to harmonize shipping. Therefore, starting today, bidding will begin, and the bids will be opened to the public in the auditorium of the County Government on the 25th. It is also reported that the committee has completed the design of the second phase of the project, which extends from Zhenjiang Pass to Xiaomatou. The design and surveying of the third phase of the project below Xiaomatou will begin now. Once the first phase of the project is completed, bidding and construction will continue.

Nantong

Investigate and Prohibit the Supply of Grain and Grass to Sea Bandits

The coastal area of ​​Jiangbei Tong is disturbed by large groups of sea bandits. Although the seaports have been blocked by military police, the bandits still use shallow waters to coerce the people to supply grain and grass. The Fourth District Security Command is now planning to thoroughly eliminate them. Under this rampant situation, on the one hand, it first ordered the troops stationed along the coast to strictly block them, and on the other hand, it strictly prohibited the people from supplying food, firewood, and grass to the bandit ships, so that the bandits would have nothing to gain.

City and Countryside Hold General Cleaning

Nantong County, both urban and rural areas, held a general cleaning on the 21st. In the city, Zheng Yitong, head of the Youth Service Corps, led 20 large teams to clean the streets by district. This cleaning campaign abandoned the parade system and adopted implementation.

President Wang Resolutely Denies Centralizing Cash

The Economy Is Indeed in a Difficult Time

The Government Will Do Its Best to Remedy It

Hopes that the United States Will Not Purchase Silver Too Quickly

According to the Central News Agency, there have been various speculations and rumors recently that the government will centralize cash and implement non-convertible paper money. President Wang happened to come to Shanghai yesterday, and the reporter made a special visit. He replied as follows: President Wang said that various rumors are nothing more than speculators creating an atmosphere, or people who do not understand the financial situation unnecessarily worrying. Most of China's silver is scattered in the hands of the people. Even if the government is willing to centralize it or reduce its fineness, what benefits would the government have? Moreover, this policy completely violates the interests of the country and the people. Therefore, no matter what, the government will never adopt it. As for the current economic problems in China, they are indeed in a difficult time. The government will do its best to remedy it. Minister Kong has recently been working hard to reduce expenditures, increase tariffs, reduce unnecessary imports, and improve agriculture, etc., which are fundamental plans. President Wang finally stated that he deeply hoped that the United States government would take into account the difficulties China is encountering when carrying out its silver purchase policy, not proceed too quickly, and hoped that it could find ways to reduce or eliminate China's current difficulties.

The Ministry of Finance and the Banking Community Negotiate to Stabilize Financial Measures

Tax Reduction on Silver Exported and Stored by Foreign Merchants

Chinese Banks Have Sufficient Currency Reserves

According to the China News Agency, since the Ministry of Finance implemented the collection of export taxes on silver to prevent large outflows, although it has been effective, domestic finance has not been completely stable. The Ministry of Finance has again negotiated with the banking community in this city on measures to stabilize domestic finance. The details are recorded below:

Reasons for Unease: According to Lin Kanghou of the Bankers Association, the sharp reduction in the reserves of banks in this port is an undeniable fact. However, upon investigation, the banks with sharply reduced reserves are all foreign banks. The reserves of Chinese banks are very sufficient and have not decreased in any way. The reason is that Chinese banks follow the government's orders and do not export silver, as evidenced by their current reserve figures. As for the recent reasons for financial unease, they are actually due to speculators creating rumors and the public not understanding the truth, which has led to silver hoarding. The upcoming New Year and tight credit conditions are also normal phenomena and are not surprising.

Negotiated Appropriate Policies: In recent years, the silver and money industry in this city has been affected by the economic downturn in society, industry, and commerce. It feels that there are thorns everywhere for those without concrete guarantees and credit relationships, and there is nowhere to lend money. Industry and commerce also feel that the market is sluggish, business is depressed, and it is difficult to gain the trust of the silver and money industry, making it difficult to borrow money to adjust finances. Therefore, the social economy is showing signs of exhaustion, which has caused general panic. In order to remedy and stabilize the financial situation, the Ministry of Finance is now holding informal consultations with the leaders of the banking community here to find relief measures, hoping to work together to develop appropriate policies that will provide concrete guarantees for the country's finances so that they can be stabilized as soon as possible to reassure society.

Chinese Banks Are Well-Funded: According to the China News Agency, since the United States purchased large amounts of silver, there have been rumors that a large amount of silver has flowed out of the city. However, according to the results of the investigation, the reserves of Chinese banks have not decreased, and the reserve funds for the banknotes they issue are very sufficient. The so-called sharply reduced reserves of banks are all foreign banks, and the export of silver is a natural phenomenon and has no significant relationship with the domestic banking community. A reporter from the China News Agency learned from the banking community yesterday that the amount of banknotes issued by Chinese banks and their reserve funds up to November are very detailed. Optimistic About the Prospects for Cooperation, Currently Negotiating Methods

Reported on the Trip's Progress to Wang and Kong Last Night

Mr. Wang expressed optimism about the prospects for cooperation. Whether or not Hu Hanmin comes north is not important. The details are recorded below:

Welcoming Personnel: Those who went to welcome him on the ship yesterday included Central Committee member Deng Qingyang, Yang Dezhao representing Chen Jitang, former President of the High Court Lin Biao, President of the Faculty of Law and Politics Wei Daoming, Appraiser Wang Huaichen from the Department of Judicial Administration, Mr. Wang's friends Tan Haiqiu, Secretary Xiao Jinfang, Zhu Yongshou (who previously accompanied Wang on his trip south and returned a few days ago), former Dutch Charge d'Affaires Dai Mingfu, Sun Danlin's secretary Yang Kenwang, and Chen Jilie and many others.

Mr. Wang Chonghui Returns to Shanghai (Photo by Zhu Shunlin)

Shanghai Shipping Companies Held a Winter Prevention Meeting Yesterday

Decided to Increase Escort Police and Implement Inspections

The Shanghai Shipping Companies held a winter prevention meeting at the Shipping Club on Guangdong Road at 2 p.m. yesterday. The attendees were the representatives of Sanbei Shipping Company, Ningshao Commercial Shipping Company, Pingan Shipping Bureau, Daxing Commercial Shipping Company, Dada Shipping Company, Datong Renji Shipping Company, Huxing Commercial Shipping Company, Ruian Commercial Shipping Company, Lianan Shipping Bureau, Jufeng Shipping Company, and Maoli Commercial Shipping Bureau, such as Chen Yisheng and Luo Lianchen. Yang Youlong, Secretary-General of the Shanghai Shipping Industry Association, attended the meeting. First, the chairman reported on the rampant piracy along China's coast and the frequent occurrence of merchant ships being robbed. In order to prevent this, following the old practice of last winter, a winter prevention meeting was held to jointly devise concrete measures. Decisive measures were taken on how to increase police escorts, how to send police to inspect, and anti-theft equipment. However, due to the fact that it concerns anti-theft, it is not convenient to publish it. However, according to a reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency, the expenses will be borne separately by the companies, and short-term escort police will be hired to patrol the docks. Passengers will be inspected before the ships set sail to prevent bandits from mixing in.

Settlement of the Songhu District Pilotage Dispute

Permission Granted for Re-examination of Previously Failed Pilots

Reduced Pilotage Rates for Vessels with Drafts Exceeding 18 Feet

Following the establishment of the Shanghai Pilotage Administration Committee, the pilotage dispute in the Songhu District has been resolved. The Committee has now granted permission for re-examination of pilots who previously failed. Pilotage rates for vessels with drafts exceeding 18 feet will be reduced. Details are provided below:

Permission for Re-examination: Pilots in the Songhu District who failed previous examinations or did not participate in the examinations organized a petition group and appealed to government authorities. The Pilotage Administration Committee has now granted permission for re-examination. As for pilots who failed the vision test, they will be given severance pay. The Shanghai Shipping Association will send representatives to oversee the re-examinations. The Association originally appointed Jia Dingxi, the owner of Changxing Steamship Company under the Sanbei Company, but because Mr. Jia serves on ships and travels不定, Chen Ganqing of the China Ship Insurance Association has now been appointed instead.

Committee Announcement: Shanghai Pilotage Administration Committee Announcement No. 5 states: For notification purposes, the Committee is currently holding pilot re-examinations. All Songhu short-term pilots whose qualifications were examined by the Committee in July, August, and September of this year and did not pass, except for those who failed the physical or vision tests, must register at the Committee's Songhu District Pilotage Office on the fourth floor of the Jianghai Customs immediately to await re-examination. Do not delay or neglect this, lest you err. This announcement is dated December 20, 1934, and signed by Chairman Kanai'er.

Reduced Rates: The pilotage rates for short-term employed pilots in the Songhu District, after being established and announced by the Pilotage Administration Committee, sparked opposition from shipping merchants, leading to a shipping strike. Subsequently, after negotiations between shipping leaders Yu Qiaqing and Yuan Ludeng, and Committee Chairman Kanai'er and Customs Superintendent Shen Shuyu, the Committee agreed to reduce rates for vessels with drafts exceeding 18 feet. Initially, shipping merchants still expressed opposition, but after mediation by shipping leaders, the issue has largely been resolved.

Strict Enforcement: The Shanghai Pilotage Administration Committee has resolved to strictly enforce the Provisional Pilotage Administration Regulations. In addition to the announcement, all relevant shipping companies are notified to comply. Anyone found to be piloting without a valid license will be prosecuted for endangering public safety and handed over to the local court for punishment. Any vessel found to employ a person without a valid license as a pilot will be fined 150 yuan in national currency.

Ministry of Finance Formulates Application Procedures for Facilitating the Circulation of National Currency

Entrusting the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications to Handle

Yesterday, a Circular was Issued to Chambers of Commerce and the Silver and Money Industries for Information

The Ministry of Finance issued a circular to the City Chamber of Commerce and the Silver and Money Industries Association yesterday, stating: In order to maintain the normal flow of finance in various regions and to facilitate commercial needs, especially during the current harvest season, merchants in various ports purchasing goods from the interior require a large amount of cash. To meet the needs of the interior, this Ministry has been issuing national currency escorts for domestic transport to various regions upon request from various banks, providing maximum convenience. However, in case of urgent needs where commercial banks cannot report in time, the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications should act as agents for remittances or transport of cash to facilitate and regulate. This matter has been discussed by the Ministry and the three banks have agreed to handle it. The three banks have replied that they have jointly formulated the consignment application form and agency transport procedures and sent them to the Shanghai Banking Association for distribution to commercial banks and to the branches of the three banks for distribution to local associations or commercial banks for compliance. In addition to separate orders, this order is hereby issued to the Association for distribution to all merchants for information. This order is issued.

City Chamber of Commerce Cables Request for Interpretation of Foreign Merchants' Responsibility to Affix Stamp Duty

Please Provide Instructions on Remedial Measures

The Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Nanjing Ministry of Finance yesterday, stating: To the Nanjing Ministry of Finance: On the 20th of this month, we received a letter from the Egg Industry Association stating that since the current Stamp Duty Regulations and Penalties were promulgated by the Ministry of Finance, all Chinese citizens within the city have been able to comply strictly. However, it is feared that foreign merchants may not be fully compliant. If a Chinese citizen purchases goods from a foreign merchant and the invoice or order form issued by the foreign merchant has not been stamped, should the invoice be penalized if it is discovered by the authorities in the possession of the consignee? If penalties are to be imposed, should they be imposed on the seller or the buyer? This is request for interpretation point one. Sometimes a Chinese citizen places an order with a foreign firm and pays a deposit. The foreign firm issues an order form, but the order form is not stamped. In the event that the price of goods rises or falls by the deadline, the foreign firm may not fulfill the original agreement, which will inevitably lead to disputes or even litigation. At that time, will the court recognize the unstamped order as valid in law? This is request for interpretation point two. The above two points are of vital interest to all industries in this city that have dealings with foreign merchants. They have sent letters to the Association requesting investigation and interpretation, which is a public sentiment. The responsibility for affixing stamp duty lies with the issuer of the document. This is the usual legal principle. In the past, except for passports and licenses issued by government offices, where the recipient paid the fees for affixing the stamps, the responsibility for affixing the stamps was borne by the issuer of the document. Therefore, if foreign merchants do not comply with Chinese laws and do not affix stamp duty, Chinese merchants have no responsibility to be penalized on their behalf. The court should be able to defend the Chinese merchant in cases of violations. Therefore, the first concern of the Association does not seem to be a problem. However, if the second instance is considered an invalid document because it is not stamped, the result is that the foreign merchant escapes tax and is exempted from fulfilling their obligations under the contract, which causes Chinese merchants to suffer a double loss. Is there a remedial measure? We respectfully request the Ministry's review and instructions for compliance in the public interest. Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce kowtows, Ke.

County Government Announces One-Year Extension of Grain Loan

The Shanghai County Government has received an order from the provincial government stating that due to the difficulties in repaying the old pre-borrowed winter grain loan in Jiangsu Province this year due to the disaster, the repayment will be extended for another year. It is reported that the old pre-borrowed winter grain loan still owes 4.5 yuan per picul. It was originally scheduled to be repaid in five years from 1930 to 1934. However, due to the provincial treasury deficits over the years, it has been repeatedly extended.
