Songpu Vessel Awaits High Tide for Another Rescue Attempt

After the Sanbei Company's Songpu vessel ran aground near Digang last Friday, it became deeply mired in the sand because there was only seven feet of water in the area, while the Songpu vessel needed eleven feet. The Shanghai head office sent the Shangjiang vessel Fuyang, along with a flatbed barge, to the vicinity of the Songpu to begin unloading the cargo from the Songpu vessel. Subsequently, it also telegraphed the Yanhufu Branch to send all of its flatbed barges to load the cargo unloaded from the Songpu. All passengers on the ship have been transferred to Hankou by the Fuyang barge. According to the crew of the Xingshi vessel, which returned to Shanghai yesterday, even after all the cargo was unloaded from the Songpu, it could not be towed out of the shallow water because the draft was still too deep. Therefore, a second decision was made to unload the ship's own coal. It is hoped that it can be towed out after the coal is unloaded, but the river water in the area has now fallen to low tide, leaving only six feet of water on the right, with no hope of getting out of the shallow water. Yesterday, according to the shipowner's report, the ship is waiting for the high tide this month to try to tow it out again. It is best if it can be rescued, otherwise it will be difficult to rescue it this winter and it will not be able to get out of the shallow water until the next spring flood season.

Shanghai Bank's Credit Small Loan Volume Greatly Increases

Currently Adding Restrictions Due to the Year-End Closing Period

Since the Shanghai Bank's Jing'an Temple Road branch started offering credit small loans, the general working class has been able to get emergency financing, and praises have been pouring in from society. Many other banks have followed suit, but their procedures are not as convenient as this bank. Yesterday, the reporter met with Mr. Xi Yushu, the manager of the bank, and had the following conversation: Reporter: When did you start offering small loans? Answer: In 1930, our bank's general manager, Mr. Chen Guangfu, initiated it and instructed the former manager, Mr. Dong Chengdao, to start it. Reporter: How do you apply? Answer: It's very simple. Anyone who lives in Shanghai and has a legitimate job, regardless of industry, commerce, education, or government, can first obtain an application form from any branch, fill it out according to the instructions, and submit it directly to this branch. Reporter: What happens after the application is submitted? Answer: After the application is submitted, the bank will send someone to investigate. Whether you are qualified or not, we can usually reply within a week. Reporter: What sectors are most commonly applying? Answer: Our bank has no preconceptions, so applicants include government, commercial, and other institutions, as well as small business owners. The amount of our loans, from 50 yuan to 500 yuan, is just right to meet the short-term needs of all sectors. Reporter: What is the amount of loans given out? Answer: Initially, during the trial period, the former manager was cautious, so not many loans were given out. From the beginning of the program to this spring, the total amount was no more than 500,000 yuan. However, I believe that in the current economic downturn, small loans are indeed a necessity to help the general working class and small business owners, so I expanded the loan amount based on the previous good results. In the past few months, the loan amount has exceeded 1.5 million yuan, and there are more than 8,000 borrowers. Reporter: With such progress, have there been any bad debts? Answer: This is inevitable, but the bank carefully investigates beforehand, and the borrowers are mostly trustworthy, so the bad debt rate is 5/1000. The current loan amount is no longer small, so this is unavoidable. Reporter: Sometimes, those who are refused loans are not given a reason. Why is that? Answer: Sometimes, the guarantor does not want to act as a guarantor. In order to maintain the friendship between the applicant and the guarantor, it is difficult to announce the reason. Sometimes it is difficult to say directly that the applicant's credit is not very reliable, so we keep it secret. Reporter: What is the success rate of loan approvals? Answer: It is difficult to set a standard. Sometimes the applicants are all reliable, so the loan is fully approved. Sometimes the results are not good, so all applications are rejected. But according to past statistics, about two-thirds of the applications are approved, and about one-third are rejected. Reporter: At this time, when the money market is tight, will your bank continue to offer small loans? Answer: I believe that small loans are intended to support those who are suffering from economic pressure and to avoid pain, so we will not stop. However, because there are too many applicants at this time, and the year-end closing period is also approaching, we will temporarily add some restrictions for the purpose of clearing the accounts.

工部局 Fire Department Report

The report from the Chief of the Fire Department of the Public Works Department for November states: during the month, there were a total of 85 alarms. Of these, 8 were false alarms. Property endangered by fire amounted to $502,093 inside the settlement and $430,500 in the special tax area. Actual losses were $128,266 and $3,380 respectively. Eleven firefighters and sixteen civilians were injured. Three people died in accidental incidents. The Fire Department's emergency ambulance received 330 alarms, resulting in 324 injured or ill individuals being transported to the hospital. Furthermore, the medical section's ambulance transported 217 patients.

Car Runs Over Villager on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Road

Car No. 6363. The injured person was sent to Minhang Hospital. Since the opening of the Shanghai-Hangzhou National Highway, cars have been traveling back and forth incessantly. Some careless drivers inevitably cause casualties. The previous day, car No. 6363 from Shanghai was traveling from Shanghai to Hangzhou when, near Caojing in western Shanghai, it knocked down a villager, Mr. Jia, from the Twelfth District of Fahua Bridge in Fengxian County. The villager suffered head injuries and bled profusely, losing consciousness. The driver, realizing he had caused a major accident, sped away. Fortunately, someone informed the Caojing section station master, who immediately used a long-distance phone call to notify the Minhang station master to intercept and detain the car. Meanwhile, the local police sent Mr. Jia to the nearby Minhang Hospital for treatment. It is said that the injuries are severe, and due to excessive blood loss, his life may be in danger.

Education, Business, and Industry Circles Preparing for Student National Goods Year

The first preparatory meeting was held yesterday at the Local Association.

A decision was made to form a joint promotion association and pass organizational guidelines.

A meeting of initiating groups is scheduled for the 24th.

The Student National Goods Year, initiated by the education, business, and industry circles of this city, including Pan Gongzhan and Wu Zhihao, held its first preparatory meeting at the Local Association yesterday evening (the 20th) at 7:00 PM. It was decided to form a Student National Goods Year Promotion Association, pass organizational guidelines and work guidelines, and hold a meeting of initiating groups on the 24th of this month. Details are as follows:

First Preparatory Meeting. The first preparatory meeting was held at the Local Association yesterday (the 20th) evening at 7:00 PM. Those present included Pan Gongzhan, Huang Renzhi, Zheng Xigu, Fang Yexian, Wu Zhihao, Yang Weiyu, Sun Daosheng, Chen Jicheng, Pan Yangyao, Ren Jinpin, Chu Fucheng, Yang Jiaoji, and Lin Kecong. Pan Gongzhan chaired the meeting, and Ren Jinpin served as the recorder. First, the chairman reported on the drafting of the organizational guidelines and work progress of the Student National Goods Year Promotion Association. Next, the agenda items were discussed. (1) The Student National Goods Year Promotion Association organizational guidelines proposal was read and revised by the chairman item by item and passed. (2) The Student National Goods Year Promotion Association work guidelines proposal was read and revised by the chairman item by item and passed. (3) The proposed list of directors was approved as is. (4) The date and time for convening the meeting of initiating groups were set for 3:00 PM on December 24th. (5) The location for convening the meeting of initiating groups was decided to be the Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA. The meeting adjourned.

Passed Organizational Guidelines. (1) This association is jointly initiated by education, business, and industry groups. Based on the year's theme of the national goods movement, it is named the Student National Goods Year Promotion Association. (2) The purpose of this association is to promote the inherent patriotism of students, awaken the public to use national goods, and unite the business and industry sectors to work together to promote the national goods movement. (3) Membership in this association is based on schools, national goods factories, national goods stores, and groups enthusiastic about national goods. Each participating member will send one representative. (4) Membership dues for this association will be freely contributed by each member. (5) This association will have a board of directors. The directors will be appointed by public discussion among the initiating groups, and the board of directors will decide to appoint committee members from among the nominated representatives to organize the following committees: A. School Committee, B. National Goods Factory Committee, C. National Goods Store Committee, D. Economic Committee, E. Design Committee, F. Publicity Committee. (6) The School Committee may establish branches within each school. (7) This association may employ staff as needed for administrative purposes, serving each committee under the direction of the board of directors. (8) The regulations for the board of directors and committees will be determined separately. (9) Matters not covered in these guidelines may be added or modified by the board of directors.

Passed Work Guidelines. (1) Realize the goals of the Student National Goods Year. (2) Assist school members in organizing and holding publicity meetings. (3) Assist national goods factories in improving production quality and increasing production quantity. (4) Assist national goods stores in promoting domestic products. (5) Assist each member in establishing national goods sales agencies. (6) Report to each member monthly on the monthly import surplus situation of the customs this year and a comparison with the same month last year.

Appointed List of Directors. The list of directors of the association has been proposed by the members and passed by the first preparatory committee meeting, as follows: Pan Gongzhan, Tong Xingbai, Wu Xingya, Tao Baichuan, Cai Zimin, Wang Yansong, Yu Qiaqing, Hu Xiyuan, Wang Xiaolai, Xiang Kangyuan, Ye Youcai, Wu Yunzhu, Guo Shun, Wu Zhihao, Huang Renzhi, Yang Weiyu, Pan Yangyao, Fang Yexian, Zheng Xigu, Yan Esheng, Xue Yuanbai, Xian Guansheng, Wang Yunwu, Lu Feibo Hong, Liu Hongsheng, Ren Jinpin, Shen Jiucheng, Fang Jiange, Zhang Huikang, Song Peidao, Xie Bingru, Shao Darren, Xiang Shengwu, Ren Shigang, Yu Zuoting, Yang Jiaoji, Sun Daosheng, Chu Fucheng, Lin Kecong, Huang Zaoxiong, Chen Jicheng, Zhu Xuefan, Kang Xuanyi, and dozens of others.

Called for Meeting of Various Groups. The association is scheduled to hold a meeting of initiating groups at the Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA at 3:00 PM on the 24th of this month. Special letters have been sent to the city party headquarters, the city education bureau, the city education association, the China Vocational Education Society, the university education association, the middle school education association, the university federation, the middle school advancement association, the city chamber of commerce, the city local association, the city federation of trade unions, the national goods factory federation, the machine-made national goods factory federation, the China Industrial Federation, the national goods maintenance association, the women's national goods promotion association, the citizens' national goods promotion association, the China National Goods Production and Sales Cooperation Association, the China National Goods Company, the Shanghai National Goods Company, the city women's association, the daily newspaper association, the family renovation association, and various schools, requesting that they send representatives to attend the meeting at that time.

The Palace Museum Embezzlement Case: Chunyun's Initial Disclosure, Xiao Xiangpei Arrested, Very Strict Custody

Xiao, a former clerk in the Palace Museum, has been dismissed.

He remained in Shanghai to hand over procedures.

According to Xin Sheng She, the Palace Museum treasure theft and embezzlement case, which was once a sensation, was initiated on October 13 of this year by the Jiangning Court Prosecutor, who collected evidence of theft and filed charges against nine people, including Yi Peiji, Li Zongtong, Chen Yu, Xiao Yu, Cui Xiebang, Yan Yuanhuai, Qin Hanggong, Dong Lin, and Zhang Songqi. Although evidence was obtained, the accused were in hiding and could not be tried. The Supreme Court sent a letter to the Ping Municipal Government to cooperate in arresting Yi Peiji and others for investigation. As a result, the news subsided. Recently, Yi's confidant, Xiao Xiangpei, was arrested in Shanghai and brought to trial. The following are the details learned by Xin Sheng She reporters.

Xiao Xiangpei's Experience in the Palace Museum. Xiao Xiangpei is from Hunan and is a fellow villager of Yi Peiji. When Yi Peiji was appointed as the Director of the Beiping Palace Museum in 1929, Xiao was summoned by Yi and entered the Palace Museum to work. Due to Xiao's honest and taciturn nature, even though he was promoted by Yi, he remained a minor clerk in the museum, earning a monthly salary of ninety yuan. Xiao did not seek more and was content with his job. When Yi was in office and embezzled treasures, Xiao was in Ping. Later, when the September 18th Incident occurred and the ancient capital became tense, the antiques were transported south, and Xiao participated in the packing work of all the antiques. Later, he followed the antiques to the south and remained in the Shanghai office, still as a clerk, with the same monthly salary, without increase or decrease.

Dismissed but Not Yet Departed. Later, when the Palace Museum treasure theft case was discovered, Yi Peiji went into hiding. Ma Heng, a professor at Peking University, took over as director. After Ma took office, he reported to the authorities that the Palace Museum had too many redundant staff and implemented a large-scale dismissal. Xiao was a confidant of Yi and his position was not important, so he was also on the list of those to be dismissed. However, because the procedures were not completed, he had not yet left the Shanghai office, even though he had been dismissed. Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, he was arrested at the Shanghai office of the Palace Museum at No. 20 Yong'an Fang. The Second Special Court ruled to transfer him to the Shanghai Local Court and assigned personnel to escort him back to the capital for trial.

Family in Shanghai in Panic. Xiao was originally alone in Shanghai. A month ago, Xiao's wife brought their three children to Shanghai and resided in the right lane of Xiaoshijie on Fuyou Road in the city. Xiao's arrest caused panic throughout the family. Because they were new to Shanghai, they were unfamiliar with the people and the place and had no way to seek help. After Xiao was arrested, Judge Xiong Huiping of the Second Special District Local Court briefly interrogated him. Due to the close connection to the major treasure theft case, the custody was very strict, and no one outside knew the details. It is rumored that Xiao Xiangpei is Xiao Yu, but this is not the case. Xiao Yu is the head of the Ping Agricultural Experiment Station, while Xiao Xiangpei is a minor clerk.

Cao Zilai Invents a Buoyancy Device to Salvage the Sunk Grand Canal Vessel

Public Demonstration Yesterday

Enthusiastic Support from All Parties

When ships sink, all countries have salvage methods, but our country has not yet invented a ship salvage device. Therefore, whenever a merchant ship accident occurs, we always ask the Japanese to salvage it. Recently, Cao Zilai, a Chinese, spent several years of painstaking effort to specialize in researching ship salvage devices, burying himself in hard work, and has now succeeded. Yesterday, Mr. Cao specially brought the invented ship salvage device to the Shipping Club for a demonstration, inviting representatives from the Shanghai shipping insurance industry to observe. The reporter also went to observe with Mr. Li Yunliang and Mr. Chen Ganqing and talked with Mr. Cao on the spot. The results of the demonstration were quite satisfactory. The Grand Canal vessel sunk outside Chongming is now being salvaged by Mr. Cao using his invented equipment, which is worth recording. Therefore, it is described in detail.

Three Inventions. Cao Zilai is from Chongming. In recent years, he has been engaged in the principles of physics and researching underwater science. After several years of experimentation and improvement, he has invented (1) a buoyancy device, which uses extremely strong materials with high strength, elasticity, and airtightness to create buoyancy devices for salvaging sunken merchant ships; (2) a sinking device, which is used to eliminate floating vessels at sea and reduce enemy ship targets during wartime; the plan has been secretly submitted to the central government; (3) a diving suit, divided into soft and hard shell types, with the soft suit especially suitable for the national character of our people to wear into the sea, which is also being manufactured. Model Demonstration. Mr. Cao's buoyancy device has been successfully developed. Recently, with the introduction of Mr. Li Yunliang, the Chief Auditor of the Recruitment Bureau, all representatives of the Shanghai marine insurance industry were invited to gather at the Shipping Club at No. 10 Guangdong Road at 1:50 PM yesterday to publicly demonstrate the ship salvage method. Mr. Cao used a large glass box filled with water and placed a specially made iron model ship in the middle. The iron content of the ship was 7.8, compared to 2.3 for the same volume of sand and mud, increasing the weight fivefold. After Mr. Cao explained the principle of the invention to the public, he connected the invented buoyancy device, which used an air bag, tightly around the sunken ship and inflated it. The sunken ship gradually floated up.

Same Principle. After the demonstration, Cao said to the public, "Today's demonstration uses a model to represent the situation. However, if a merchant ship sinks at sea, using this method to salvage it would require a larger ship body, and the air bag used for buoyancy would naturally also need to be enlarged. In fact, there is resistance." Cao said again, "One cubic foot of water weighs 62.4 pounds. According to this, an enlarged air bag, composed of steel wires, is sufficient to overcome this buoyancy force and can be completely successful." Assuming we are salvaging a 1,600-ton sunken ship, Cao said that he is very confident in the salvage, and the estimated cost is only 10,000 yuan.

Trying to Salvage a Sunken Vessel. The Grand Canal vessel, which travels between Shanghai and Chongming, has been sunk for many years near Chongwaibaochen Port. The ship was not insured and has not been salvaged. Now, Mr. Cao has volunteered to salvage the ship using his invented ship salvage device and has contacted the shipowner. The shipowner is willing to pay a salvage fee of 32,000 yuan to entrust Cao with the salvage. Various Shanghai insurance companies have expressed extreme support for Mr. Cao's actions. The Nantong County Government and the County Party Headquarters have also raised the issue at 23 meetings, and County Magistrate Jin Jiahua and Standing Committee member Chen Guanying have publicly decided to unanimously support and encourage him.

Cotton Industry Statistics Association Releases National Cotton Production Statistics Yesterday

Imports of Foreign Cotton Are Gradually Decreasing

New Cotton from This Year Has Not Yet Arrived in Shanghai

China's cotton production this year has increased by more than 10% compared to previous years. Imports of American and Indian cotton have sharply decreased. According to the national cotton production statistics released by the Cotton Industry Statistics Association yesterday, the cotton production quantities for 1933 and this year are excerpted as follows:

Decreasing Imports. According to the Cotton Industry Statistics Association's statistics last year, the national cotton production was 9,774,207 dan. This year's second estimate is 11,172,553 dan of ginned cotton. Compared with last year, this year's production has increased by 1,398,346 dan. In 1932, Chinese yarn factories used approximately one million large bales of American cotton. As of the first half of this year, foreign cotton imports have gradually decreased, now falling to 170,000 bales. It is predicted that the number will be even lower in the second half of the year. There are three reasons for this: (1) American cotton prices are high; (2) exchange rates are too expensive; (3) China's cotton production has increased. Therefore, from January to October of this year, imports of foreign cotton were approximately 1.4 million dan. The total for the entire previous year was approximately 2 million dan. The reason for the decrease this year is that domestic cotton production has increased. Subsequent imports will decrease year by year.

Total Cotton Consumption. According to statistics from the Chinese Yarn Factory Federation, the total cotton consumption of yarn factories nationwide in the second half of last year and the first half of this year is shown in the following table:

First Half of 1934 Second Half of 1933

Chinese Cotton 919,279 841,709

American Cotton 175,652 341,366

Indian Cotton 88,306 97,060

Egyptian Cotton 8,449 9,828

Other 1,166 328

Total 1,192,852 1,190,290

The above figures are in bales, each weighing 500 pounds.

New Cotton Not Yet Arrived. Among China's cotton-producing regions, Shaanxi, Shandong, Hebei, and Hunan provinces have the largest production. Cotton is usually available on the market around October. In previous years, a large amount arrived in Shanghai. This year, however, it has not been seen, which has surprised those in charge of various factories. After sending personnel to investigate, the truth became clear. There are four reasons: (1) This autumn, there has been much rain in the north and severe drought in the south, causing cotton growth to be slower, 20 days to a month later than in previous years; (2) This year, cotton farmers in the north and northwest have had good harvests of barley in the previous year, and cotton production is also abundant this year. The wheat they are currently growing is also good, and the economic situation is good. They are not in a hurry to sell cotton, so there are very few selling on the market, and it is all hoarded by the villagers to seek a good price; (3) Although cotton prices are higher this year than in previous years, the villagers are greedy and unwilling to sell, all engaging in speculation; (4) New cotton-producing areas, such as Lingbao in Shaanxi, have inconvenient freight car allocation on the Longhai Railway, so it is all stockpiled in warehouses, waiting for empty cars to travel south. Due to these several reasons, the new cotton of this year has not yet arrived in abundance.

Jiangsu High Court Borrows Shanghai Court to Retrial Li Guojie Case

Security Very Strict

Listening Seats are Full

Li Guojie, the former general manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, was involved in an embezzlement case in September of the year before, involving a huge amount of 700,000 taels of silver. After the case was discovered and the local court conducted the first trial, Li Guojie was sentenced to three years in prison for breach of trust. Li refused to accept the judgment and appealed to the Jiangsu High Court. As a result of the second trial, the charge was changed to embezzlement, and the sentence was increased to three and a half years. Li still refused to accept the judgment and appealed to the Supreme Court. Li was still sent to the Shanghai Hospital at the Nantao Wharf in Nanshi for treatment due to illness, which has been for more than a year. The Supreme Court has now remanded the case to the Suzhou High Court for retrial and has officially scheduled the hearing for December 21st at the Shanghai Local Court. This information has been reported previously. Yesterday was the scheduled date. At 1:00 PM, Chen Junfang, the judicial police chief of the Local Court, and Chen Xihui, the police officer, went to the Shanghai Hospital to escort Li Guojie to the court. Meanwhile, the West Gate Branch dispatched patrol officers Nie Chaowen and Dai Mingkai, police chief Su Xianyao, and eight police officers, as well as detectives Yu Ruhai, Zheng Yongxiang, and Bian Wenguang, to escort and care for him along the way to show caution. The Suzhou High Court assigned Presiding Judge Hu Shanjie, Judges Si Wen and Zhang Zepu, Prosecutor Shen Bingqian, and Clerks Shen Yuren and Ding Yi to come to Shanghai by car. The general public who wanted to listen to the hearing first obtained hearing tickets from the High Court at the entrance before being allowed to enter the court to listen. However, this case has attracted much attention from society, so the listening seats were full. The judicial police chief Chen Junfang, the police officer Chen Xihui, and many bailiffs under the supervision of Patrol Officer Nie maintained order around the courtroom. At 1:30 PM, Presiding Judge Hu, along with Judges Si and Zhang, and Prosecutor Shen, took their seats in the first courtroom. Private prosecution attorneys Wang Youling and Li's lawyers Jiang Yiping, Lu Hongyi, and Lu Shifang arrived in court one after another. Presiding Judge Hu ordered Li Guojie to be brought to court. (Li was wearing a dark wool coat, with a medicated plaster for a headache on his temple, and looked dejected and spoke very softly.) He stated that he was 54 years old, from Hefei, Anhui, and lived on Haining Road. (Asked) "How is your illness?" (Answered) "My limbs are numb and have not yet recovered." (Asked) The official said, "Now that the Supreme Court has remanded the case for retrial, you should provide a detailed account of the situation." (Answered) "Since taking over as the general manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company in 1932 and concurrently serving as the chairman of the board, I intended to develop and reorganize everything. The loans were secured by more than 17 or 18 mu of land on North Sichuan Road, such as Jinliyuan Wharf, and five wharves including the North and Middle Warehouses and the Pudong Yangjiadu China Warehouse, mortgaged for a total of 20 million taels." (Asked) "When were the loan documents signed?" (Answered) "I was ordered by Supervisor Chen Fumu to sign on behalf of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company as the general manager and chairman of the board on September 5th and 6th of 1932. (Asked) "Do you know Wang Jusu?" (Answered) "He was Chen Fumu's representative. The 700,000 taels of checks were taken by Wang Jusu on the orders of Chen Fumu." (Asked) "The amount of 700,000 taels is very large, why did you hand it over so easily?" (Answered) "That night, I called Chen Fumu, but he was out, so I went to Chen Fumu's house the next day and met with Chen. According to Chen, the receipts would be processed and given to me later. I thought I should obey the orders of my superior. I thought that after receiving Supervisor Chen's receipt, I would then register the account, but unfortunately, this happened. Because Chen Fumu was the Deputy Minister and Supervisor, I did not suspect him. Earlier, Chen Fumu called me and said that he ordered Wang Jusu to come and take the money and would replenish it with official business later." Then, witness Dou Yaoting, 43 years old, from Yin County, Zhejiang, who worked as a comprador in the American-owned China Trading Company, testified that the loan contract for the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company was handled by the manager and directly contacted Li Guojie. On September 23, 1932, the manager ordered me to send the 700,000 taels of checks to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and hand them over to Li Guojie, around 3:00 or 4:00 PM. When I entered Li's office downstairs at the time, Li Guojie seemed to know my intention. There were a total of fourteen checks, and Li issued a receipt from the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. (Asked) "Did you see Wang Jusu?" (Answered) "I didn't notice. I didn't sit down and left." At this point in the hearing, Li Guojie stated that Wang Jusu was also present at the time. (Asked) "Does Li Guojie know the current addresses of Chen Fumu and Wang Jusu?" Li (Answered) "I don't know." Attorney Jiang stood up and stated that Chen Fumu and others were far away overseas and would definitely not come to court and requested that Li be allowed to post bail. The official said, "The matter is of great importance and cannot be approved." The case requires investigation and will be heard again later. During the interrogation, Li Guojie could not stand for long due to illness, so he was instructed to sit and answer questions. After the court adjourned, Police Officer Chen Xihui escorted Li Guojie in a car back to the Shanghai Hospital for continued surveillance. Patrol Officers Nie and Dai led the police officers and detectives in separate cars to escort them, to avoid any negligence.

Continuing Record of Yi Fangshuo's Trial

Yi Baozhu and Li Xiaozhen Suddenly Unwilling to Accuse

Defendant's Request for Bail Rejected by Judge

Yi Fangshuo, a native of Hangzhou residing at No. 147, Baxianfang Entrance, Huage Nie Road, French Concession, who performed comedic plays at the New New Company rooftop amusement park, was arrested for repeatedly raping his cousin Yi Baozhu (19 years old) and monitoring her movements. On the 11th of this month, Baozhu seized an opportunity to escape and reported to the French police, who dispatched detectives to arrest Yi. They also brought in thirteen young actresses from his troupe for questioning. It was further discovered that Yi had sexually assaulted Li Xiaozhen, his concubine Yi Meimei's thirteen-year-old sister. He was ordered to be detained, and the next day, he was sent to the Second Special Court for interrogation and investigation, as detailed in previous reports.

The police investigation concluded, and at 11:30 AM yesterday, Judge Zhang Chaozu presided over a continued trial in the First Criminal Court. Nearly a hundred family members and friends of Yi Fangshuo were present in the audience. After the court opened, the defendant was brought in and briefly questioned about his name and age. Then, police lawyer Fei Xizhen presented the case, stating that the police investigation revealed that Yi Baozhu was adopted by the defendant's uncle, Yi Fusheng, as his daughter at the age of two. When Yi Fusheng and his wife passed away when she was eight, she was raised by the defendant's stepmother. In November of last year, the defendant sent a letter to his mother, requesting that Baozhu be sent to Shanghai to learn acting from him. On the second day after arriving in Shanghai, the defendant allegedly lured her out on the pretext of getting her teeth fixed, taking her to a hotel and raping her. Afterwards, the defendant had his concubine, Wang Caitao, and others monitor Baozhu's movements. Baozhu also witnessed the defendant raping Li Xiaozhen. The police are now prosecuting him under Articles 240, 243, and 316 of the Criminal Law for offenses against public morals and infringement of freedom. The investigation also revealed that the defendant bought and sold people, purchasing Yi Jinzhu for 150 yuan and Yang Linmei for an unknown price. The police are also prosecuting him under Article 257 of the Criminal Law, requesting legal action. At this point, the court declared the hearing closed to the public.

After the audience members left, the defendant Yi Fangshuo was questioned about the rape of the two women. He denied it, claiming that Yi Jinzhu was introduced to him by Chief Ye of the Zhejiang Water Police as a maid who wanted to learn acting at his place. Yang Lindi was his cousin's younger sister who was brought to be the adopted daughter-in-law of his nephew, and she was sent to his house to learn acting. As for the monitoring, he claimed that he was their acting teacher, and because there were many kidnappers outside, and he was afraid they would be hit by vehicles on the road, he sent people to accompany them. After the performance, he would order them to go home and not allow them to go out.

The judge then summoned the complainants, Yi Baozhu and Li Xiaozhen, who both stated that they did not wish to accuse him and requested permission for a peaceful resolution. Yi Baozhu's guardian, Yi Hu (the defendant's stepmother), and Li Xiaozhen's father, Li Duofu, also hired lawyers who tearfully stated that they all depended on the defendant for their livelihood and did not wish to accuse him, requesting permission to take the girls back. The judge then asked the police for their opinion. Lawyer Fei stated that Articles 240 and 243 of the Criminal Law require prosecution by complaint, and since the complainants had withdrawn their complaints, the police had no objections. However, the court had the right to conduct a trial for Articles 257 and 316. The judge then summoned Yi Jinzhu and Yang Senzhu, but they did not appear, so the trial could not proceed. The court then announced that the hearing would be adjourned to the afternoon of the 24th. The defendant's defense lawyer requested that the defendant be granted bail to await trial outside of custody, but the judge ruled that the case involved human rights and public morals, and the circumstances were severe, so bail could not be granted. He ordered the defendant to remain in custody. Yi Baozhu and Li Xiaozhen were temporarily allowed to be taken away by Yi Hu and Li Duofu. The judge ordered that the two girls still had to appear in court on the adjourned date and could not leave, and after being taken away, they could no longer reside in the defendant's home. Yi Hu and Li Duofu acknowledged the order and took their daughters away before leaving the court.

Woman Sues After Becoming Pregnant Following Three Years of Cohabitation and Half a Month of Marriage

Impending Childbirth Requires Funds

Former Husband Denies Paternity

Zhang Guiying, a woman from Guangdong who is 28 years old, is of unremarkable appearance and stout build. Most of her relationships are temporary, leading to frequent separations and reunions. Three years ago, she became romantically involved with Chen Jianxun, a fellow villager of similar age. Initially, they were very compatible. By April of this year, both felt the need to formalize their relationship through marriage. They soon chose an auspicious date for the wedding. However, their informal cohabitation lasted three years, but their formal marriage lasted only half a month, from April 24th to May 16th. There may be no shorter-lived marriage in the world.

Now, the woman's belly is as big as a five-stone urn, and childbirth is imminent. She claims that the child in her womb is Chen's, and although they are divorced, Chen should still be responsible for the cost of childbirth. She sued Chen in the First Special District Local Court, requesting a judgment ordering him to pay 200 yuan for childbirth expenses. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Qiao Wanxuan opened the court to hear the case. According to the woman's testimony, she and Chen had been cohabiting for three years, and she had given birth to a son last year. However, after their marriage on April 24th of this year, Chen gradually tricked her out of all her gold and silver jewelry, leading to her abandonment. He drafted a divorce agreement and gathered ruffians to force her to sign it. However, her pregnancy is nearing term, and she requires funds for childbirth, which she requests the defendant to pay 200 yuan. Chen Jianxun admitted to the court that he had initially cohabited with the woman, then married her, and finally divorced her by signing an agreement. However, he denied that the child in her womb was his and claimed that he had already provided financial support at the time of the divorce and had no ability to provide additional funds. Zhang Guiying then asked the court what to do after the baby was born. Judge Qiao replied that this was another matter and that if there were any disputes in the future, a lawsuit to confirm identity should be filed, which cannot be predicted now. As for this case, he advised them to go out and reconcile. If a peaceful resolution is ultimately impossible, the court will reconvene on the afternoon of the 28th of this month for further hearing.

One on Peng Road, One on North Jiangxi Road

Both Parties Receive Supreme Court Judgment

The property lawsuit involving the Shanghai Yimiao Dianchuntang estate, which began last July between the Seafood and Grocery Trade Association and the Sugar Trade Association due to claims of joint ownership, has concluded. Tongde Submits Written Report on Harvard Ship Incident

According to Guowen News Agency, the Shanghai Maritime Affairs Bureau of the Ministry of Communications received a report from Dafaxing yesterday regarding the collision between the Tongde ship and the Harvard ship on the 17th. The report was based on the "Nautical Log." The captain of the Tongde ship, Norwegian An Kierxun, also submitted a similar report, which was countersigned by the ship's first mate, Qu Zhenbang, as a witness. The original report is as follows:

On the 17th of this month, at 8:20 AM, [we] left the Zhonghua Wharf to go to Qingdao. The ship was completely empty, intending to transport coal from Qingdao to Longtan. [We] were sailing north along Pudong. At about 8:56 AM, [we] saw a little of the bow of the Harvard ship. Because [we] were at the bend of Lujiazui, near the Pudong side, [we] could not see the entire ship, even though [we] were only two or three ship lengths away. I immediately sounded a long horn to warn the other ship, but the other ship did not respond. About half a minute later, [we] sounded a short horn to indicate that [our] ship was sailing to the right. The other ship also responded with a short horn. However, the other ship was still sailing head-on. At that time, the tide was rising, and [our] ship was moving very slowly, but because [we] were being pushed by the tide, [we] were still moving. Seeing that the other ship did not give way, I immediately sounded three short horns and reversed the engine at full speed. After about two or three minutes, the bow of the Harvard ship collided with the bow of [our] ship. The location was very close to the Water Police Lighthouse ship. [Our] ship was still reversing. The Harvard ship, being pushed by the tide, continued to move forward. The bow of the ship sailed southwest, dropped anchor, turned its head, and ran aground on the beach at the Chunjiang Wharf (outside the city ferry terminal). [Our] ship immediately dropped anchor. At 9:10 AM, [we] raised the anchor and sailed to Yangshupu, between buoys 45 and 44. This is the truth.

Qingnian from Pinghu Attempts Suicide by Jumping into the River

Sent Back to His Hometown by the Fellow-Villagers Association

Qian Huangcheng from Pinghu, 16 years old, was formerly a student at a certain lumber company. Recently, due to unemployment and economic reasons, he had the idea of committing suicide. Yesterday, he boarded a boat and jumped into the Huangpu River. He was rescued by the Water Patrol Team of the Municipal Public Security Bureau and transferred to the Pinghu Shanghai Fellow-Villagers Association for disposal. It is heard that the association, fearing that he would attempt to jump into the river again on the way, specially sent someone to accompany him back to his hometown and hand him over to the Pinghu Public Security Bureau to visit his family and receive him.

Abusive Woman Held Awaiting Sentencing

Chen Wu, a Guangdong woman, 28 years old, who lives at No. 723 Tiantong Road, is habitually tyrannical and has no children. Last summer, she spent 50 yuan to buy 12-year-old Xu Xingbao, a girl from Changshu Meili Township, in name as an adopted daughter, but in reality as a slave. Initially, because of her young age, the treatment was not bad. In the spring of this year, she began to have her do the work of a servant. The girl was not up to the task, and with a little negligence, she would be brutally beaten, using wooden sticks and rattan canes to inflict painful beatings. Recently, she has become more ruthless. If the girl did not wash clothes cleanly, she would use a small hammer to knock her hands, the most horrific instrument. She would heat up a clothing iron and burn the girl's back and waist, causing the girl to be covered in injuries, as if she were in a fiery pit. At about 9:00 PM on the 18th, Ms. Chen ordered the girl to go to the nearby coal stove to get hot water in a thermos. She accidentally broke the bottle and did not dare to go home, fearing being burned with a hot iron. She cried sadly on the road. Patrolman No. 469 of the street police inquired and learned the whole story. He took the girl to the Hongkou Police Station, and Chen Wu, along with the wooden sticks, rattan canes, hammer, and iron, were escorted to the First Special District Court for interrogation and detention. A forensic doctor examined Xu's injuries in detail. Yesterday, Judge Wu Zehan opened the Criminal Court No. 3 to hear the case. The court read out the forensic report, which stated that the girl had many wooden stick and rattan cane injuries on her arms and legs, of varying degrees of bruising. The back of her hands and fingers had fractures from being hit with a hammer that had not yet healed. Her back and waist had obvious burns from an iron. Questioned about it, Ms. Chen's testimony was evasive. She insisted that she had only used wooden sticks to beat her. Lisi Shan, a lawyer for the Bureau of Public Works, stated that the weather was very cold, and Xu was only wearing a tattered pair of single pants with holes in her lower body. Her feet were bare. The areas burned by the iron were already inflamed and likely to fester. The defendant was cruel and ruthless and did not treat her as an adopted daughter. She was regarded as a slave and abused to this extent. She had no regard for the law, human feelings, morality, or humanity. Please punish her severely. Judge Wu ordered Chen Wu to be remanded in custody and scheduled for sentencing. Xu was sent back to the Jiliang Institute to stay.

He Weixu Sues Estranged Wife for Cohabitation

He Weixu, 24 years old, a native of Ningbo and former employee of the Asia Electric Company, who lives at No. 484 Baoding Road, married Liu Wanzhen (21 years old), a woman from Zhenhai who resides at No. 18 Xiudeli, Beck Road, through a matchmaker on October 31st of last year. The couple's relationship was quite harmonious. In June of this year, she gave birth to a child, who is now three months old. However, on October 23rd of this year, Liu suddenly returned to her mother's house. After several months, He hired a lawyer to file a petition with the First Special District Local Court, requesting a judgment ordering Ms. Liu to cohabit with him and return the clothes and jewelry she had taken. Yesterday morning, Judge Luo Chongtai opened the Civil Court No. 7 to hear the case. According to He Weixu's testimony, the reason for the defendant's departure was that in December of last year, the defendant took jewelry, etc., to her parents' house, which I found out about. I rebuked her for not obtaining my consent. On October 23rd of this year, I ordered the defendant to take back the jewelry, and she abandoned her three-month-old baby and left suddenly. Therefore, I request a judgment ordering her to cohabit with me. Questioned about it, the defendant Liu Wanzhen testified that since she married into the family, the plaintiff's brother had contracted syphilis, and her mother-in-law blamed her for having bad luck. Not long after entering the family, the eldest brother contracted a malignant disease, and she was constantly scolded. She could no longer bear to cohabit. She had filed a separate lawsuit for divorce. The defendant's father then testified, stating that since his daughter returned to Ningbo on October 23rd, because the weather was getting colder, he accompanied his daughter to retrieve her clothes on the 26th, but the plaintiff reported it to the police and had him detained. Judge Luo advised them to reconcile in court, but it was unsuccessful. After ordering the start of the debate, he announced that he would issue a judgment at a later date.

Shanghai Oil Pressing Industry Association Petitions to Maintain Northeast Soybean Oil Tax Rate

The Shanghai Oil Pressing Industry Association, regarding the import tax on Northeast-shipped soybean oil, sent a telegram to the Yuan Ministry on the 11th, requesting that the original plan be maintained. Since no reply has been received, another telegram has been sent to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, requesting relief. The telegram is as follows:

Respected Chairman Chiang of the Nanchang Headquarters,

We respectfully submit that our country's import tax originally set the tax rate for commercial goods at 15% of the value and for food oils at 30% of the value. It has been found that the initial import tax levied on Northeast-shipped food soybean oil was 15% of the value. The subsequent correction of the mistake to 30% of the value was extremely fair. This was to avoid the dumping of goods from the Northeast, manipulating the economy, and protecting our country's industry and commerce. The intention was excellent. However, recently we heard that some people were taking the opportunity to oppose it, presenting a request to the Ministry of Finance to change the tax on food soybean oil to be taxed as commercial goods. After the association learned of this, it sent a telegram to the Executive Yuan, Ministry of Finance, and Ministry of Industry, requesting that the original order be maintained. However, no reply has been received, and the community is extremely anxious.

It has been found that soybean oil has always been a major food item in our country, and it is rarely needed for industry and commerce. If the previous order is restored, the Northeast will inevitably continue to dump and manipulate [the market], which would violate your Excellency's advocacy of national products. Moreover, our country's industry is nascent. If Northeast goods are allowed to destroy it, it would not only lead to the bankruptcy of oil factories, but also to the desperation of workers' lives. Therefore, in addition to continuously sending telegrams to the Yuan Ministry and making a request, we respectfully believe that your Excellency cares about the national economy and protects the people's livelihood. Members of the association are tearfully submitting our appeal, and we look up to your Excellency to review and quickly order the Ministry of Finance to maintain the import tax on Northeast-shipped food soybean oil as before, without changing it. This would increase the source of national tax revenue and save the livelihoods of hundreds of thousands of oil industry workers. National interests and people's welfare all depend on your benevolent implementation. Looking up to the sky, we are endlessly fearful and urgently await orders.

Respectfully,

Zhu Jingan, Chairman of the Shanghai Oil Pressing Industry Association

Farmers in the Southern Shanghai District Request Subsidies for Transporting Night Soil

The southern district of Shanghai connects to the city, and there are more than 200 night soil carts used by farmers in the area. These are all poor farmers who push and transport night soil from the city to be used as fertilizer. Therefore, although this is a cleaning job, it is completely voluntary and receives no compensation. After the January 28th Incident, the economy has not yet recovered, and this year there has been a severe drought, while the price of vegetables is very low, with green vegetables worth less than two copper coins per pound. As a result, farmers have no way to make a living. Considering that the sanitation workers receive a monthly reward from households, ranging from two dimes per household, a meeting of all cart owners was held at Jiangjing Temple in Xiaomuqiao yesterday to resolve the matter. They requested subsidies from residents to balance their incomes.

Central Bank Inspection Report

No. 218

The Central Bank's 218th Inspection Report on Issuance Reserves states: "In accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Charter, this committee is responsible for inspecting the bank's issuance of convertible currency reserves. The 218th inspection was conducted at the bank on December 20, 23rd year of the Republic of China. The inspection results are announced as follows:

(A) Total amount of convertible currency issued: 87,497,383 silver dollars, including: 81,126,837 silver dollar notes, 6,229,106 auxiliary currency notes. Total amount of convertible currency reserves: 87,497,383 silver dollars, including: 69,319,383 silver dollars in cash reserves. This cash reserve includes: 64,400,665 dollars stored in the bank's issuing vault, 2,993,766 dollars stored in branch offices in various ports, 1,918,952 dollars stored with correspondent banks. Guarantee reserve is equivalent to 18,178,000 silver dollars.

(B) Total amount of customs gold convertible currency issued: 373,324.70 customs gold units. Total amount of customs gold convertible currency reserves: 373,324.70 customs gold units. This reserve includes: 7,351.95 taels of standard gold, which, at a fixed price of 5.0779, is equivalent to 373,324.70 customs gold units.

According to Article 1 of the Central Bank's Convertible Currency Regulations, cash reserves should be 60% and guarantee reserves should be 40%. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserves exceed 60% and the guarantee reserves are less than 40%, which is in accordance with the regulations. This report is hereby made.

Chairman Li Fusun of the Supervisory Committee of the Central Bank, Supervisors Xie Mingxun, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, and Xu Jilun, December 21, 23rd year of the Republic of China.

Medical News

Seeking Good Doctors and Prescriptions Gu Futang's letter seeking a good doctor says: My wife is now 39 years old and has a history of liver yang syndrome. When it occurs, her hands and feet are numb and cold, she has dizziness and stagnation of qi, and even confusion. She has given birth eight times in total. The first five times were safe, the sixth time was a miscarriage, and the seventh time was also safe. The eighth time was in early September of the lunar calendar last year, and it was also a miscarriage. Three days after the delivery, due to a slight smell of carbon monoxide, her liver yang syndrome relapsed and became increasingly severe. After treatment with both Chinese and Western medicine, she improved slightly until this spring. By summer, she was able to sit up, move around, and her appetite improved. Later, she had several Western-style massages and more than 40 Chinese-style massages, but they were ineffective. Two months ago, she was introduced by a friend to a hospital in Pudong for treatment. Because she caught a cold in the hospital, she became heavier again. After being discharged from the hospital, she was treated by Chinese and Western doctors and ancient-style Jin Zhenke doctors, and she improved slightly. However, on the 3rd and 4th of this month, it worsened again. Her appetite is poor, she cannot sleep day or night, and her chest and abdomen are sometimes spasming, and sometimes her hypochondria are painful. Sometimes her abdomen is full and distended, causing headaches. Recently, confusion has been added, and her limbs are weak. Medication is ineffective. Both Chinese and Western doctors say that it is caused by physical deficiency and that she needs to rest in order to recover. According to the current situation, I am afraid that rest alone cannot save her. I don't know if there are any other methods. If you can give high-level guidance, or give a prescription, or indicate a famous doctor, if she can be healed as a result, then my wife and I will feel like we have been reborn. Gu Futang, December 15th, Communication Address: Accounting Department, Continental Press, Telephone 15426.

Letter to the Editor

Sir, yesterday I read the local news in your newspaper about the collision between the Continental Merchant Shipping Company's export ship and a junk outside Wusongkou. After reading it, it was inconsistent with the facts. According to the junk named Jin Liyuan, the owner of the ship is Liu Tong. The location of the collision that day was in Wusongkou, opposite Yun Cao Bang, at the northern head of the Pudong Beach Customs buoy. Furthermore, the weather was clear and there was no fog at all. This is a tragic incident involving a collision. I am sending you this letter to request your editor-in-chief to quickly correct it to clarify the truth and respect humanity. I cannot express my expectations and gratitude. Sincerely, Liu Tong, shipowner of the junk Jin Liyuan, December 21st.

Education News

Liaoning Education Decimated Under Brutal Japanese Rule

No Education to Speak of in Jinpu and Other Areas of Dalian

(Northeast News Agency, Shenyang) Since the brutal Japanese occupation of the Northeast, they have paid close attention to education. In addition to destroying the original education, they have continued it with enslaved education. The following is a summary of the educational situation in Liaoning Province.

(Increased School Dropout Rate in Dalian) The western part of Dalian, under the jurisdiction of the Shaohekou Police Department, including Xishan Guildhall, Xishahekou, Sanchunliu, Xianglujiao, Xinmintun, Mazhangtun, and other places, although industry and commerce are developed and it is close to Dalian City, the population has increased accordingly. The number of children enrolled in school should also have increased greatly. However, there are only two ordinary schools in the area, Xishan and Houjiagou, and the school buildings are extremely narrow and cannot accommodate all students. Therefore, the number of school-age children is increasing day by day. In the new semester of this year, the number of boys and girls volunteering to enroll in these two schools reached more than 900. Among them, only 300 were able to enter the two schools, and the remaining 600 were almost all out of school. From this, it can be seen that in Dalian, which the Japanese have occupied for a long time, the restrictions and destruction of education are because they are afraid that Chinese people will also have knowledge, and they are indeed implementing a policy of ignorance.

(Education in Jinpu and Other Areas) In recent years, in various elementary schools in Jinzhou, Pulandian, and other places, because there are many graduates and few secondary schools, most of them have no place to go to school and end up dropping out of school. It is found that in the new semester of this year, the number of students who graduated from various elementary schools in the state who did not get promoted was huge, exceeding the past. At the moment, those concerned about education in Pulandian, Piziwo, Jinzhou, and Lushun have specially contacted various elementary schools and other merchants, etc., and elected representatives to petition the Japanese puppet authorities, but the result is still unknown whether they will refuse or even allow the implementation of enslaved education.

China Public School Student Declaration on the Dancing Ban

Advocating Actively Improving the School Environment

Hoping that University Students Will Automatically Remind Each Other to Abstain

Regarding the issue of banning university students from dancing, since the previous city education bureau issued a circular to major middle schools, it has attracted attention from all walks of life. Students from China Public School in this city specially issued a declaration to respond. The school's ethos has always been very simple and the student movement is also very active. It is heard that in order to implement their views on the issue of banning dancing, the students of the school plan to unite with schools in Shanghai to further discuss it. The contents of the declaration are excerpted as follows: Since the Union of Universities in this city proposed banning university students from dancing, newspapers have reported it, turning it into gossip, and people in society have not examined it deeply, and have arbitrarily hyped it up, as if university students are all frivolous people. This kind of mistaken view not only has the suspicion of insulting the personality of university students, but also is enough to hinder the progress of Chinese university education, and what is the adverse impact on the future of the nation? Furthermore, we university students, as intellectuals, know how to love ourselves and are especially unwilling to lightly degenerate and invite contempt. Even if there are occasional visitors to dance halls, they are only a small minority. Moreover, the infection of this bad habit is actually a reflection of social pathology. Since it is not an innate endowment, it is mostly caused by the temptation of the environment. The way to treat it is definitely not just to hold a negative ban to be effective, it depends on actively improving the school environment, subtly influencing it, guiding it according to the situation, so that students regard the dormitory as a home, in order to cultivate the habit of frugality and diligence in study. The measures stipulated in the recent letter from the City Education Bureau to the major middle schools, such as "installing friendship venues to reflect educational films, promoting proper entertainment, and strictly implementing military training," are practical ways to get to the root of the problem. "Principals and teachers of various schools must never visit dance halls" is an urgent task. I deeply hope that the authorities of various schools will lead by example and implement it effectively, so that the grass will fall when the wind blows, and the atmosphere will be able to be transformed. I, the nation's university students, tell all of our university students that university students are the foundation of the country and the nation. Our actions are a model for society. At this time of national crisis and national peril, we should especially reflect on the difficulties of the times, hone our ambitions, and strive to strengthen ourselves. Not only should we absolutely abstain from dancing to advocate for society, but also, all bad habits must be automatically abandoned and reminded of each other. If there are any deliberate violations, we should lead them as a harmful horse and abandon them with everyone, in order to establish social faith, promote the new life movement, and create a bright future for our university students themselves. The nation's revival depends on it. We are not sensitive and will definitely practice what we advocate to the end. We wish all of our students in the country to rise up together and plan for it. This is our declaration, and we hope that you will give it your consideration. More than 120 students from China Public School, Luo Yiwen, Chen Manhua, Wang Jiashu, Chen Zongli, Shui Xiangyun, Fang Youcong, Liu Jinxing, Wei Duanmin, Huang Jinhua, Huang Jinsheng, Hu Guoguang, etc.

New School Building for the Municipal Council Chinese Girls' High School Completed

Moving in February

The Municipal Council's Chinese Girls' High School, currently located temporarily on Avenue Road, has had funds allocated by the Municipal Council to build a new school building in the Singapore Road Park. The construction has now been completed, and it is scheduled to move in at the beginning of the spring semester. The new school building is a three-story building, with the eastern and western ends being four stories high. The structure is made of reinforced concrete frames with brick walls and an exterior of colored coatings and specially made brick surfaces.

The east end of the ground floor houses the gymnasium and auditorium, equipped with a stage. One side has folding partitions that can be opened to connect to the corridor. The auditorium is two stories high, and above it is the dining hall, which can accommodate 150 people. The kitchen and service room are located on the upper level of the dining hall, equipped with a service elevator for transporting food. Next to the kitchen is the cooking classroom.

The west end of the ground floor houses the washroom, boiler room, and staff room. The library is on the upper floor, and the manual arts room and physics and chemistry laboratories are on the third floor. The upper floors all have flat roofs that can be used for recreational activities.

In front of the building, to the south, is a spacious lawn. Next to the main entrance, in addition to the janitor's room, there is also a bicycle and rickshaw storage room. In total, the school is equipped to accommodate 500 students, with 21 classrooms, all with south-facing windows. The school is currently accepting new students. Registration is still at the old location on Avenue Road. The registration period ends on January 14, the examination will be on the 18th, and the new semester will begin in the new school building on February 1.

Furthermore, the Municipal Council's Penglu West Girls' Public School has merged with the Hambury West Girls' School to become the Hambury West Children's Public School and has built a new school building at 1 Haining Road, scheduled to move in on January 7.

Yuqing Petitions the Bureau of Education

According to China News Agency, Yuqing Middle School and Jinan Affiliated High School fought for the final spot in the Middle School Group of the Middle School Sports Federation at Shen Garden the other afternoon. Yuqing defeated Jinan Affiliated High School 3-1, resulting in a bloody tragedy after Jinan resorted to violence. The details were reported in yesterday's newspaper. More than 300 students from Yuqing Middle School went to the Municipal Bureau of Education to petition yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM. Section Chief Chen Bai responded that he would investigate and resolve the matter.

Jinan Apologizes, Both Sides Reconcile

According to another source, the cause of the incident was minor. Near the end of the game, Jinan team member Shi Yongnan accidentally kicked Yuqing player number 14 once while trying to gain possession of the ball. One side did not mean to do it, while the other side intended to retaliate. Therefore, just as the whistle blew to end the game, Yuqing player number 14 suddenly approached Shi Yongnan and kicked him violently. Jinan team member Zeng Rongzhong, fearing that this would cause trouble, ran forward to dissuade him. However, player number 14 thought that Zeng's arrival was malicious and suddenly ran towards his classmates. The cheering squads on both sides misunderstood and each showed their skills, resulting in a chaotic and tragic fight. Afterwards, two representatives from each side went to the Caojiadu Public Security Bureau to report the incident. Yesterday, the Jinan authorities, fearing that the misunderstanding would deepen and the situation would escalate, and that newspapers were falsely reporting that students at the scene had knives and guns, specially sent Secretary-General Chen Rongding and Director of Education Situ [name obscured] to Yuqing to apologize and explain the misunderstanding. The physical education instructor of that school, Yu Hengzhi, also sent a separate letter to the National Sports Association to express his apologies. This disturbance has been amicably resolved after understanding between the two authorities. As for what the Shanghai Secondary School Sports Federation will do about this matter, it will not be expressed until after a report is received and a meeting is convened.

Mayor Wu Addressed the Ceremony and Presented Awards

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education held the awards ceremony for the third Municipal Secondary School Sports Meeting at the City Hall at 2:00 PM yesterday. Mayor Wu, Director Pan [name obscured], Huang Zaoxiong, representative of the Municipal Party Committee, Ma Chongyu, Shao Rudong, Wang Keyong of the Education Bureau, and more than 100 athletes from various schools attended. The chairman was Pan Gongzhan, and the master of ceremonies was Yuan Zengyu. Mayor Wu gave a speech and presented the awards. The details are as follows:

Chairman's Report: First, Chairman Pan Bureau Chief reported, stating that today is the awards ceremony for the third Municipal Secondary School Sports Meeting. 本届运动会参加田径者七十七校运动員九○九人、团體操三十三校三十七节、会操三十五校二千七百人、总计参加五千四百余人、其人数及成绩均较过去进步. This year, 77 schools participated in track and field with 909 athletes, 33 schools participated in gymnastics with 37 sections, and 35 schools participated in team exercises with 2,700 people, for a total of more than 5,400 participants. Both the number of participants and the results have improved compared to the past. Today's award ceremony is just to encourage middle school students to pay attention to Physical Health, and it is not what the sports meeting focuses on. Therefore, those with poor grades should not be discouraged, but should continue to practice. What is especially important is that athletes must have sportsmanship, noble character, and restrain themselves from engaging in out-of-bounds behavior. They must recognize that trophies are just a tool, and improving Physical Health is the goal. In the past, unfortunate incidents have often occurred, such as yesterday's soccer game, where fights broke out. This kind of improper means and irregular methods are a disgrace. Everyone must encourage each other so that such wrong actions do not occur, etc.

Mayor's Address: Next, Mayor Wu gave a speech, saying: According to Director Pan's report just now, this year's results have improved compared to previous years, which is very gratifying. Students often hear me say that China's hope lies in the youth of China today, and China's destiny rests on the youth of today. Therefore, I have great hope for the youth, so I cannot help but constantly supervise and urge them, hoping that you can prepare everything in your youth so that you can shoulder the great responsibility of the country in the future. China has a long history of more than 4,000 years, a population of 440 million, and a vast land and abundant resources, which are unmatched by other countries. Therefore, China's future prospects are very promising. Today's youth are the rising stars, the awakened youth. If they can work hard and prepare their knowledge and skills, I believe that one day they will definitely be able to turn China from weak to strong. Director Pan also said just now that athletes often engage in out-of-bounds behavior. We know that sports are not only Physical Education, but also cultivate a selfless spirit and consider the interests of the team, not just one's own. This kind of spirit must be cultivated during student days, so that when serving in society in the future, one will not be selfish, etc. Then, Huang Zaoxiong, the representative of the Municipal Party Department, gave a speech, hoping to (1) Popularize Physical Education so that every student can participate in sports and have a healthy body; (2) In addition to sports, military training should also be emphasized, etc.

East Asia Defeats Nanxing in Basketball Friendship Match

Twenty-nine to twenty-five

The East Asia Technical College basketball team, since its organization this semester, has been practicing with various strong teams in Shanghai. The night before last, it surprised everyone in the charity match, defeating Jinnan University, the strongest Chinese team in Shanghai, with a score of 25 to 21, demonstrating its strength. Each player is strong and powerful, and with further training, it will not be difficult to become the most promising elite team in Shanghai. Yesterday, taking advantage of the victory, the team played against the Jiaotong University athletes of the Nanxing team at the Jiaotong University gymnasium.

At the beginning of the match, Nanxing was very agile, with Chen Hu and Liu Jiang scoring consecutively. East Asia was not to be outdone, immediately retaliating, resulting in a 4-4 tie. From then on, the two teams exchanged points, remaining evenly matched. The first half ended in a 13-13 tie. As the second half began, East Asia gradually took the lead, with its defense being particularly good. Nanxing also did not relax, and both sides put on a wonderful performance. As a result of the intense battle, East Asia won the final victory with a score of 29 to 25.

Bank Club Billiards Finals

Zhao Zihui Wins Championship

Last Year's Champion Xu Junyi Retreats to Runner-up

The Bank Club members' handicap billiards final was held at 5:30 yesterday. The finalists were Xu Junyi and Zhao Zihui, with Hu Yunlai as the judge. Many spectators attended, including directors and staff of the club, Lin Kanghou, Yang Dunfu, Zhu Zhuanghua, Yao Yongli, as well as members and guests. Zhao Zihui started the game first, and Xu Junyi scored 35 points after several attempts, while Zhao only had 14 points at the time. However, Xu subsequently missed several shots and gained nothing, while Zhao gradually caught up, and the score gradually narrowed. Before long, Zhao surpassed Xu and took the lead smoothly. Towards the end, although Xu had a huge score of 47 points in one shot, Zhao already had 221 points at this time. After a few more shots, Zhao won the championship and ended the entire game. As a result, Zhao scored 250 points and Xu scored 214 points. Xu's highest score was 47 points, and Zhao's was 20 points. The handicap standard was 300 for Xu and 250 for Zhao. Securities Long-Short Swap, Public Debt Fluctuations Mixed

Yesterday, in the Shanghai Chinese Securities Exchange, because there were only two or three days left for the futures in this month, the long-short swap transactions were quite active. No. 16 was the wide-head swap or supplement, No. 41 was the long-head swap, and the rest of the scattered swaps were not lonely. Therefore, although the foreign currency overnight interest rate increased to four jiao, the trend was still very strong, and the number of buyers gradually increased. Short covering such as Nos. 48 and 53 was also considerable. Although the money supply was tight, it was a temporary phenomenon. Retail investors bought and arbitraged because it was more generous and stable than ordinary deposit interest rates, so this type of transaction also accounted for a part of the power, and the future can be stable. In the past yesterday, the morning opening was because the foreign currency overnight interest rate continued to rise, and there were quite a few sales, and the front row slightly decreased by two or three jiao. After the entry, because the large short position of No. 16 was slightly hedged, people's sentiment turned to rise, so the rear row rose by one or two jiao, and the whole six were uniquely good at four jiao. In the second round, short positions continued to be hedged and swapped, and the market price uniformly returned to strong, mostly increasing by five points, one jiao to four jiao. Nos. 48 and 53 had stronger buying interest on the market, while Nos. 4 and 11 had sales. In the afternoon opening, No. 41 was a long-head swap, No. 16 was a short-head swap, and Nos. 14 and 38 also had sales, and the trend became chaotic again, with highs and lows mixed. Only reorganization was uniquely good at four jiao, and the rest fluctuated by one or two jiao. There were still many swap transactions at the closing, and the market price was slightly tired by one or two jiao to three jiao. The trends and prospects were mostly based on the relationship between the more or less chips, and they were mutually squeezed out, but most of them have been prepared, so the fluctuations have been limited. The market price results were mostly mixed, and the number was only two or three jiao. The situation seemed to be more squeezing out short positions than squeezing out long positions, so most of them were high near and low far. Grain and Flour Markets See Reduced Factory Selling

Yesterday in the flour market, after the morning opening, the market for each month presented a relatively stable appearance. The quoted prices for foreign wheat ranged from a little over a quarter to less than a quarter, depending on whether it was from Chicago or Canada. At the opening, because the delivery date for this month was approaching, many outside longs were engaging in liquidation, so the opening price showed a softening trend. Trading in distant months was very light, temporarily showing mutual restraint. (The outlet for current flour from northern firms is still active.) Approaching the afternoon opening, trading in each month was still not brisk. Factory chips were uncertain due to undelivered foreign wheat, so they were selling less. The market trend showed no improvement, but it was also difficult to decline. It remained hovering as usual. Recently, customer sales have shown signs of fatigue. This month fell by 1 fen, January fell by 1 fen and 2 li, February fell by 7.5 li, March fell by 1 fen, April fell by 2.5 li, and May was unchanged.

Flour trading is suspended from today until the 26th of this month for national accounting. Normal trading will resume on January 3rd of next year.

Longs Liquidate for This Month's Wheat

Yesterday in the wheat futures market, after the morning opening, the market for each month generally presented a flat and weak state. The quoted prices for foreign wheat ranged from a little over a quarter to less than eight fen. Trading in each month was still sluggish at the morning opening, with prices slightly lower than the previous day by 1 or 2 fen. By the afternoon opening, because delivery was approaching, longs for this month were liquidating one after another, while hedgers mostly watched and did not move, so prices became looser. This situation is really due to the year-end closing, reducing speculation inside and outside the industry. As a result, this month fell by 4 fen, January fell by 5 fen, and February fell by 2 fen. Because traders have not acted, the current wheat market is still inactive.

The Miscellaneous Grains Exchange will close its books according to the Gregorian calendar. Trading for this month's wheat will be suspended until the 26th, while trading for all other distant months will be suspended until the 29th of this month. Normal trading will resume on January 3rd of next year.

The winter wheat planting area in Chicago is estimated at 44,360,000 acres, with crop conditions at 77.8% of normal. New wheat from Australia and Argentina will soon be exported in large quantities. Although the market will not experience a major reaction, buyers are mostly taking a wait-and-see attitude.

Year-End Erie Rice Prices Slightly Weaken

Yesterday's foreign rice market saw weak demand for spot goods from both local and customer appetites, hindered by the year-end closing and the relationship with silver. However, futures were strong both domestically and locally, because autumn harvests in Jiangsu and Zhejiang were not good this year, and many hoarders were hoping for good prices. However, foreign merchants were also actively selling off, and the pressure to sell was even stronger recently. Yesterday, they opened up to sell 1,400 tons of broken rice and 100 tons of returned small rice. In addition, they also telegraphed from Yaxing regarding the eggplant rice from Lan Huang, estimated to have 2,000 tons of rough rice for February at a price of 4 yuan and 6 jiao and 6 fen, and 1,500 tons of polished rice for March at a price of 5 yuan, 1 jiao and 2 fen. Because the combined price was both cheap and suited the tastes of the domestic market and Shaoyong, it attracted the attention of the industry. It is said that it had already been distributed domestically and locally in the afternoon. Currently, 800 packages of foreign rice have been opened, and customer glutinous rice is popular locally. 8,760 packages have been opened, and the market price has weakened slightly by 3 to 5 fen due to the year-end.

If purchases continue, and sources decrease, the prospects are optimistic. Sesame prices from foreign firms continued to fall by half a jiao. Sassoon took 500 packages at a price of 9 yuan and 05 fen. The main reason is the tight silver situation, and merchants are selling cheaply, so it is feared that the market will not easily recover within the year. Spot trading in the market is also light, and market prices have fallen by another 4 to 5 fen.
