Shen Bao Local Supplement Movie Special

Reasons Why Women Want to Be Performers

— Suyin

Everyone wants to be on stage or screen

Naturally good at pretending and imitating

"Women all over the world, deny it all you want, but if you use a microscope to examine you, you can see that every one of you has a thought in your mind to be a performer." The above is what an American star said. Of course, this situation is definitely true in America. When they are six or seven years old, they see Shirley Temple and want to be Shirley Temple themselves. At sixteen, they might want to be a small Vampa star, like Patrice Aries, showing off. At twenty-six, they want to be Joan Crawford or Jean Harlow. Even when they are over fifty, May Robson is their good example. As for those over sixty, it's the former Marie Dressler. Still did a movie queen after sixty? In the screen, the age limit can be said to be absolutely unique.

Female students, female salespersons, female receptionists, social women, professional women, family women, they all have the same thought - want to show off in the warm mercury lamps or behind the lamps. Performing, internal pretense, that is the most difficult and hard thing in the world, but if she is determined to be a female actor, she will go forward without hesitation, and no sacrifice or hardship can stop her from moving forward. Helen Hayes started performing on stage at the age of eight. Until now, her theatrical career has not stopped. Someone asked her why women have that kind of indomitable spirit. Helen smiled and said, "Why? Why do little girls who are not even big run to the empty room upstairs, find a silk dress, and dress up as a young lady? Isn't this a woman's natural psychology of imitation and acting"? But in order to act, to imitate, she is not afraid of hard work. Like Helen Hayes on the sound stage, surrounded by lights on all sides, so hot that she can't breathe, she still has to take pictures on the left and right. Isn't that too unworthy? But according to Helen Hayes, just dressing up and imitating is attractive enough.

But Lancel Dolores has a different view. Her view can be represented by a few words, that is, "Silver Fox Coat". Lancel Dolores said: "You all know that silver fox fur coats occupy a very important position in the minds of women. Well, if you want to wear a silver fox fur coat, you have to find a way to make money, and the best way to make money is to be a female actor! Diamonds are also women's favorite things, their weaknesses. In order to wear diamonds as jewelry, there is no better way than to be a female actor". Lancel's words are of course also a kind of experience. When she was a receptionist at the Grauman's Chinese Theatre, she had neither a silver fox fur coat nor diamond jewelry, but she was born a movie fan, and the movie star she admired the most was Gloria Swanson. She thought that being a receptionist at the Grauman's Chinese Theatre was the best place to be, because that was where Hollywood stars gathered. When leading them to their seats, she could either touch the silver fox fur coat they were wearing, or she could attract their attention, because she was born very well. Sure enough, she attracted the attention of others, and got a silver fox fur coat. Recently, she married a millionaire, and she can buy as many diamonds as she wants. Isn't this the reason why women want to be performers?

However, the desire of many women to be performers cannot be simply explained by "silver fox fur coats" or "diamonds." Several female actors' families were originally very wealthy. Some might as well find a wealthy millionaire to marry him, wouldn't that allow them to ask for anything they want? Therefore, Carole Lombard said: "The reason why women want to be female actors is because women want to be independent. Being a performer is the best way for them to be independent." You can rely on your beauty to coax your husband and ask him to take out money to make new clothes for you, but, Carole Lombard said: "How many women in the world are really happy to coax men and ask them to take out money to make new clothes? Wouldn't they rather have their own money and make their own new clothes? Being a performer is the way for women to be economically independent. She has her own money, so she doesn't have to bow her head and ask for help." According to Carole Lombard, not only can female performers be economically independent, but also housewives should be given salaries by their husbands every month, which is the remuneration they deserve for managing household affairs, so that they have the ability to be economically independent, so that they have their own money to buy clothes, shoes, socks, pocket money, etc., and do not need to reach out and smile to ask their husbands for money.

Of course, what is said above is not enough to include all the reasons why women want to be performers. Some are born with the ambition to be performers, and some use the shortcut of being performers to attract men. And being a performer also has a broad interpretation. Many ambitious women, although they do not go on stage or screen, can use the secrets of being performers to sensationalize society and influence politics. These cannot be explained in detail here.

Movie Review

Review of "Treasure Island"

— Luo Ping, You Jing, Ling He

Treasure Island 丨 Nanjing 丨

Following several literary and artistic films, we have now watched the performance of "Treasure Island."

"Treasure Island" is a novel loved by the world, especially by children. It is even used as an English textbook in Chinese schools. Taking this opportunity to see it again on the screen, it is naturally a pleasure for us to have a deeper understanding and a more profound review of it.

Here, I feel it is necessary to briefly analyze the author first.

Robert Louis Stevenson was born in Edinburgh in 1850. He fought poverty and disease throughout his life and died of lung disease on the remote Samoan island in the Pacific Ocean at the age of forty-four. He was an optimist. In the face of poverty and illness, he always lived bravely and happily, feeling joyful like "a king" as sung in his own poems . Until his death, he even wrote his own epitaph: "Under the wide and starry sky, Dig the grave and let me lie. Glad did I live and gladly die, And I laid me down with a will."

Stevenson regarded life as just a game, in which we must play very seriously, always hoping for victory in a disciplined manner, and never despairing.

He was very talented in literature, using realistic groundwork and romantic techniques (transitioning from romanticism to realism) to depict the postures of various people in various places in a very delicate and moving way.

In his youth, he wrote stories about the Bible to tell his companions. In addition to "Treasure Island" and "Kidnapped," novels loved by children all over the world, there are legends such as "The Master of Ballantrae," "David Balfour," and ethical novels such as "Dr. Jekyll and Mr. Hyde." There are also three volumes of short stories such as "New Arabian Nights," "The Dynamiter," and "Merry Men and Other Tales and Fables."

In the evolution of literature, Stevenson was quite behind compared to the writers of his time. While realism had become the main trend of the literary art at the time, he was still wandering between realism and romanticism, yearning for and reflecting the style of Scott. It was only the discovery of American literature that changed part of his writing methods. Similarly, his imaginary stories, he only wrote in a more bizarre and spicy way than the previous generation to make them more interesting.

Collins was able to describe a rogue. Where their evil deeds were heard, they were so personified that they became such grand and special villains, that the reader could not help but feel a natural pity. Such a villain is Count Fosco in Collins' "The Woman in White," and Long John Silver in Stevenson's "Treasure Island."

Obviously, from Jim's perspective, we can see Stevenson's subjective opinion:

In the relationship between the nobility (earls) and the commoners (pirates), the author uses the child Jim to convey his own views. In addition to maintaining the noble class, he also interestingly gives the pirates, even the villains, a personality of sympathy. After listening to Long John Silver's memories of pirate life and the tragic pain of hanging, Jim felt "the meaning of being in the same boat and the respect for adventurers," and humanely let him escape. As he said in his "The Sire de Malétroit's Door," "Two hours of life is two hours," and in the last paragraph of "Treasure Island," Long John Silver's theft of gold nuggets shows that "a pirate is still a pirate." The meaning of works such as "Robinson Crusoe" mainly lies in the initiation and encouragement of colonial aggression, and "Treasure Island" also undertakes this task in the same way. Regarding Smolle's erection of the British flag on the desert island, saying, "This is British land," and Jim's mouth saying, "God Save the Queen," when he pulled down the pirate flag. Also, regarding Long John Silver's farewell to Jim, saying, "You will have a bigger ship in the future, and you can discover more gold and silver," this is the way out the author pointed out to young people like Jim.

In terms of performance, "Treasure Island," like other literary and artistic films, only managed to faithfully adapt the original work.

Not at all harshly, Victor Fleming here did not relax his use of sound film techniques, but did not have a particularly great success either. Naturally, in this film, he has a heroic spirit, majestic rhythm, and solemn atmosphere, all of which cannot but coerce the audience's emotions. However, the earth-shattering power of "Don Quixote" or "Viva Villa!" is lacking in this film.

As for personal acting skills, the previous performances of Warner Oland, Lionel Barrymore, Jackie Cooper, and Lewis Stone can be guaranteed. In particular, Lionel Barrymore's scene when he first entered the hotel is particularly excellent due to the director's handling of the atmosphere. Others are omitted here due to space limitations.

Review of "The Crime Doctor"

— Shi Fu

"The Crime Doctor"

丨 Grand Shanghai Screening

This is a more meaningful murder detective case. From the script, it can open up new paths, have the spirit of a detective film, and interweave the philosophy of love. Roughly, there is a famous detective who wants to divorce because his wife loves someone else. On the surface, he is aware of the fate of love, but secretly he is jealous. So he hires a woman to secretly investigate the actions of his rival in love. Unexpectedly, this woman plans to blackmail his rival. Unfortunately, his wife finds out and asks him to handle this matter. So he borrows a knife to kill, steals his rival's gun, and beats the woman to death, making a plan to shift the blame to harm his rival. Because the arrangement is professional and thorough, the result of the investigation is that the rival is convicted. Even more unexpectedly, his wife believes that her lover is innocent and asks him to find a way to solve the case, and promises that if he can solve the case, she will not marry again, and is willing to stay with him forever. But this makes the great detective stuck. He also realizes that the fate of love is certain, so he has no choice but to confess and then commit suicide.

What the script gives us to ponder is that such a meticulous and calm great detective would not hesitate to commit crimes for jealousy. And if a woman loves a person wholeheartedly, no matter how much power you have, do not think about saving her. Although these things are not necessarily justified, if there is one of them, it can create the material for this film, let alone all of them. So in this script, it looks very simple on the surface, but in reality there is a lot of drama to be made.

The director's technique is very experienced, and there are very few redundant parts. Especially in the scenes where Detective Ford arranges the murder, it is straightforward and does not reveal the tragic state of the victim from beginning to end, which is also extraordinary. The dialogue is concise. The scene in the courtroom is very solemn and tense. Actor Otto Kruger's performance is calm and profound. The selection of the two female roles is also appropriate. There are no dull moments, but the most boring thing is the ending, which is a bit superfluous.

Star Monthly Vol. 2, Issue 5 Published

"Star Monthly," edited and published by Star Film Company and distributed by Renji Luahua Trading Company, Volume 2, Issue 5 has been published. It contains sixteen pages of exquisite copperplate images, divided into photos of new films, star life, work activities, and so on. In terms of text, there are articles by Bao Shi, Shu Yin, Bai Si, Hua Ling, etc., beautifully printed on Taolin paper in Song typeface. The price is two corners per issue, and it is sold by newspapers, magazines, and bookstores.

Movie Novel

Bigamy (2)

— Dai Zhou

The money wired from his hometown to Shanghai made Wen Hua more depraved! Because he wanted to marry the socialite Xiang Qin, and prepare rings, etc., he sent a telegram home, asking for two thousand yuan, saying that he was going to become an official, and with two thousand yuan, he could take office. Wen Hua's father hurriedly sold all the accumulated grain and mortgaged the land, scraping together two thousand yuan and wiring it over. Wen Hua received the swindled money, rented an extremely luxurious house, and married the socialite Xiang Qin. The two sweetly slept on a wire bed. A month passed, and Wen Hua's parents in his hometown were extremely anxious amidst Wen Hua's sweet honeymoon. The neighbors all came to ask when Wen Hua would take office. The old people could not help but worry secretly: "It has been more than a month, why hasn't there been any news about Wen Hua taking office?" They sent a letter but received no reply. Wen Hua's mother anxiously said to her husband: "You should go there yourself! So you don't have to ask someone to write a letter! What is going on?" Like a heavy piece of lead, it pressed tightly on the hearts of the two old couples. Wen Hua's father took the train to Shanghai to find Wen Hua, found the private Yadong School of Law and Politics, but the messenger told him that Wen Hua had rented a house at No. 32 North Henan Road. He managed to ask his way along the address, and found a luxurious and novel Western-style house. He timidly patted the iron gate, and a young female servant flashed out from inside: "Who are you looking for?" Looking at his empty, ragged short coat and pants, he quickly said: "I'm looking for Huang Wen Hua, I'm his father, I have something to talk to him about." Wen Hua had already gone out. The female servant took him to see the hostess, the socialite Xiang Qin. At this time, she came out dressed. Seeing the ragged clothes of the person in front of her, which were beyond her expectations, she coldly spat out a puff of cigarette: "Are you Wen Hua's father? Where do you live? Wen Hua has gone out and hasn't come back yet." He told Xiang Qin that he was staying in a Shanghai hotel, and if Wen Hua came back, please tell him.

At the door, he met his son. Wen Hua was walking towards this side. Seeing his father, he was shocked and hurriedly dragged his father away. Xiang Qin saw Wen Hua's embarrassed appearance from the turret, and she suspected that Wen Hua must have lied to her. She hurriedly changed into a cheongsam and chased him to the Shanghai hotel, opened a room next to Wen Hua's father, and eavesdropped on Wen Hua's father's voice through the crack in the wall: "When are you going to take office? The money at home is almost used up, your wife..." From these words, Xiang Qin felt that Wen Hua had indeed deceived her. She angrily left the Shanghai hotel. Late at night, Wen Hua returned with a relieved face. Xiang Qin deliberately asked with a smile: "Who was that country bumpkin who came today?" Wen Hua was embarrassed for a moment, then smiled and said: "That's my family's servant, he came to ask me to go back and divide the property. Oh, I have to tell you, I have to go back to my hometown!" The day after Wen Hua returned home, Xiang Qin chased him to this Fanchuan Village. At that time, many villagers were congratulating Wen Hua on becoming an official. She walked into the house, and met Wen Hua's wife, Xiu Feng. Seeing Xiang Qin's strange clothes, she hurriedly asked: "You're looking for Wen Hua, who exactly are you to Wen Hua?" Xiang Qin looked at Xiu Feng straightforwardly and said: "I am his wife, we got married in Shanghai." Xiu Feng's face suddenly turned pale when she heard this: "Then you have been deceived by him, I am his wife, we have been married for almost a year!"

Two lawsuits were opened in the solemn courtroom: Xiu Feng accused Wen Hua of abandonment, demanding a divorce and compensation of five thousand yuan. Xiang Qin accused Wen Hua of bigamy, demanding compensation for losses of ten thousand yuan. The judge asked Wen Hua: "Do you admit it?" Wen Hua nodded miserably and was imprisoned, sentenced to one year and six months. He miserably recalled the past. This irreversible depravity! The family went bankrupt; the savings of his father's decades of sweat and blood, and the son's dream of studying and succeeding were also shattered! He shed tears, sadly pacing on the field ridges——

The scenery of Fanchuan Village is still as beautiful as a poem, shrouded in the slanting rays of the setting sun. (The End)
